side this bozra that say city there arose even naples the side parthenope new town kartha chadtha contraction karchadta from which the greeks made out the town for perhaps two hundred years increased but slowly paid tribute the libyan peoples and was for long time state dependence upon tyre towards this her mothercity carthage was never wanting filial piety not even when its relations her had completely changed which one the fine traits her history the time when carthage began extend its sway know nothing placed was the midst barbarous nations which were not able amalgamate with could not have risen into prosperity quickly the greek colonies the asiatic coasts where races men were dwelling between which and the pelasgian stock there was affinity although not language yet that spirit refined humanity which distinguished them for instance the lycians and carians who even before they were hellenized had already attained considerable degree civilization see from their monuments and institutions the carthaginians not betake themselves husbandry and therefore they could not multiply fast families which spread out the libyans were hard oppressive neighbours barbarians berbers they are called this very day who only gradually mingled with the phnician settlers was not
until the middle the third century rome more than three hundred years after her own foundation that carthage made her appearance power the earlier times are shrouded impenetrable darkness justin gives some notices from trogus but most carelessly does also diodorus who all likelihood borrowed from timus the former has account war and conquest carthage malcus one its generals certain that carthage for long time paid tribute the libyans and the first sign its vigour the throwing off this yoke hardfought struggle particularly favourable carthage seem have been the fortunes the mother country phnicia which after having long and painfully striven against egypt yielded itself persian protection for though indeed its condition was thus tolerable enough yet times foreign yoke was felt galling and many may have then emigrated the free colony which was made thrive the more tyre owing its connexion with persia now became the port for the whole asia even far india the treaty with rome the year the city shows that the carthaginians were then already masters part sicily sardinia and libya that they were great people for that age about the year they are said have come over with army men into sicily against gelon
syracuse and theron agrigentum this however not real history pindar and simonides sang the achievements gelon and theron but history was not yet written not that such expedition has never taken place what doubtful the assertion that happened the same time the invasion xerxes the battle himera said have been fought the very day that was defeated salamis but the other hand the better chronological statements which rest upon the authority timus show that gelon who supposed have conquered himera came the throne later date than that the battle salamis the expedition the carthaginians must have happened the olympiad and must have been insignificant they were beaten and not for long time think again undertaking anything against sicily they now strengthened themselves other quarters when the athenians engaged their enterprise against sicily hear little nothing the carthaginians they were confined motye panormus and solois the first which three places phnician settlement yet when the expedition had come such unhappy end the implacable revenge wreaked against segesta and the other cities which had welcomed the athenians now brought the ruin sicily these cities applied carthage which sent considerable army over all the greek towns were involved the greatest danger selinus agrigentum
camarina gela and other places were destroyed dionysius the elder concluded disadvantageous peace but was afterwards more successful the reign dionysius the second the carthaginians renewed the contest timoleon defeated them and drove them back motye and lilybum yet the peace the old status quo was reestablished and the western part sicily remained their hands the rivers nimera and halycus continued the boundaries which thenceforth were looked upon the normal ones and were generally restored when peace was made the days agathocles the carthaginians besieged syracuse but second campaign during which motye was destroyed and they were for some time confined lilybum they were compelled restore the boundary the himera then followed the events the times pyrrhus who carried out the plans agathocles still further after his departure the carthaginians spread themselves again and afterwards got possession once more agrigentum the beginning the first punic war carthage was mistress the whole the western half sicily and the northern coast far messana africa her rule extended the corner the great syrtis nearly the whole the territory tunis was subject her along great part the african coast there was number carthaginian colonial towns there were likewise several them the interior for the

the year the third the war the romans undertook besiege agrigentum with two armies this town was great extent yet city was but mere shadow what had been hundred and forty years earlier before its first destruction the carthaginians within its high and strong walls considerable army the enemy had now thrown itself the name the punic general was hannibal the carthaginians were called their firstnames only and one might easily led think that they were all related each other there were few these names hannibal hanno hamilcar and some others these correspond our christian names the roman prnomina gaius they certainly had all them family names also which however that time were not yet made use designate individuals they had even byenames but these have been partly lost the generals who bear the name hannibal are the whole carthaginian history insignificant when set beside that great man who gave the name its renown that little mention only made them hannibal had posted himself with fifty thousand men within the wide and waste precincts agrigentum the two consular armies advanced the south against the town entrenched themselves two camps and constructed two lines against the city and against any one
who might attempt relieve the carthaginian generals were very bad the beginning the war they either made use all the elephants only limited one and they were very loth give battle the romans hannibal had now imprudently allowed himself thus hemmed and agrigentum does not lie close the sea could not get any succours from thence yet succeeded conveying the carthaginians single messengers and letters his entreaties for relief they indeed when had been besieged five months sent hanno with large army and fifty elephants this general pitched strong camp near heraclea took erbessus the arsenal the romans and means barricades felled trees shut them that they were much distressed for want supplies and account the state health their troops for the carthaginians were masters the sea and the numidian horsemen the cossacks the ancients made exceedingly difficult for them forage seemed they would obliged give the siege and retreat yet they could not bring themselves showing this instance also their perseverance and the contrary they kept the blockade strictly that hannibal found means bettering the condition his troops when under these circumstances two months had gone hanno may have had reasons attack yet the romans gained complete victory and
set themselves again the booty which they got his camp all this time hiero had given them every possible help without him they would have perished hannibal who had been brought extremities took advantage the moment when the romans were enjoying themselves the night after their victory make preparations for sally the soldiers filled the ditches the roman lines with fascines and sacks straw climbed over the ramparts drove back the outposts and thus fought their way through all that the romans could was annoy them the rear whoever was able bear arms got off this way but the inhabitants the town were for the most part left behind well the sick and the weak agrigentum was the following morning sacked and pillaged like town taken storm here the romans made for all their privations the whole the unfortunate population was swept away after this frightful event year passed without any remarkable occurrence the carthaginians strongly provisioned and fortified their other stations the west yet they also acted the offensive their fleet cruised off the coasts italy which laid waste the northern coasts sicily likewise surrendered their power from fear whilst the romans kept the inner island and the eastern
coast the conquest agrigentum gave the latter quite different ideas with regard the war formerly they merely wanted have messana and syracuse dependent allies but now their object was drive the carthaginians altogether from the island dionysius agathocles and pyrrhus had done they saw however that this could not done without fleet was the same difficulty athens where the peloponnesian war and the times immediately following they had other ships but penteconters lembi and triremes with from men who were partly rowers and partly marines and with deck the penteconters which had men were open and the benches for the rowers both were placed across before and above each other these vessels had been outdone long since and larger ones were needed syracuse the cradle mechanical art quadriremes and soon afterwards quinqueremes were first mounted ships larger class which were not round and which might properly called ships the line for the difference the triremes and quinqueremes cannot have consisted merely the number the benches and the rowers but must really have been the build itself otherwise great skill would have been required construct them these quinqueremes had already for long time been use especially the macedonian sicelian and punic
fleets but neither the romans nor the antiates had them the romans had also triremes and wherever the antiate vessels are mentioned they are triremesthe oars had the same effect our steam boats being independent wind and tide the ancients could however sail very well besides quinquereme had three hundred rowers and hundred and twenty marines these rowers the triremes could oppose but hundred and twenty who therefore were able little against them frigate brigantine would against ship the line this accounts for the statement that the romans had had fleet all and yet they had built triremes for the passage sicily they wanted therefore model from which the ships might built correct principles that they could worked with ease and they might certainly have sent for shipbuilder greece egypt ptolemy philadelphus with whom they were already allied and have fetched model thence for the ancients indeed built from models but happened that carthaginian ship war was driven ashore and from they built hundred and twenty quinqueremes these were indeed very unwieldy and the romans had not the number sailors which they wanted that say more than they were therefore obliged man them with levies from the inland districts and
with slaves the russian ships are conscription the interior the empirefor the seamen from etruria and the greek towns were means sufficient polybius goes too far stating that they had had able seamen all these were trained ply the oars upon scaffoldings dry ground this drilling told seems utterly ridiculous and the carthaginians must have been altogether unlike our nations this occasion whole crowd caricatures were not published among them there was those times the same contrast between roman and carthaginian ship which there nowadays between russian and english american man war but the romans being great this they were all things devised the means overcoming this disadvantage their fleet was unable make head against the carthaginians the ordinary tactics and was very likely that very time and not later one that the idea was conceived ridding the seafight all artificial evolutions and rather making ship fight against ship for required the greatest skill manage and steer the ships against wind and tide the same way rider manages his horse shatter the enemys vessel means the rostrum and tear off the benches the rowers this was more than the romans dared think wherever enemy met who greatly superior skill the
only way conquering employing masses some unexpected invention thus carnot gained the victory for the french opposing masses the thin lines the enemy the battle wattignies oct the turning point the modern history warfare the end the old and the beginning the new tactics general hoche had recourse the same system lorraine masses the americans also beat the english ships which otherwise they would have never succeeded doing the romans invented boardingbridges made wood which were wide enough for two men run upon abreast and protected both sides railings the prow every ship large mast was set resting which the bridge was drawn aloft the upturned end having iron ring through which hawser was passed the bridge was raised lowered windlass and fastened itself the hostile vessel means grapplingiron thus the advantage superior skill which the carthaginian rowers possessed was done away with the romans moreover had their best legions board and all likelihood the carthaginians had only middling bad marine soldiers these were not picked this was the year according cato according varro the first attempt was not however successful the beginning all the ships were not yet armed this manner squadron was caught great disadvantage near the liparian

the other hand order resist them the expectations every one were riveted upon this undertaking just the times the spanish armada the most important points the northern coast sicily were still the possession the carthaginians and provisions had taken syracuse the romans not venture sail round lilybum but they preferred the way round pachynus between that headland and agrigentum the carthaginians met them with the whole their fleet the roman ships being still unwieldy the result depended before the use the boardingbridges they had hit upon strange disposition their ships were divided into four squadrons each which had one legion with its brigade allies and number transports the two first squadrons sailed form two sides triangle angle the two admirals being placed side side and therefore with their rostra standing out towards the sea the base the triangle was formed the third squadron which advanced straight forwards and had the transports tow behind these sailed the fourth squadron which was cover the rear the two first were each commanded consul the third and fourth other leaders whom not know any thing further they therefore formed which the attack the enemy manuvre for the execution which great many favourable circumstances are
requisite and the ships which other times used sail straight line diverged and made wedge illustration the numbers the squadrons the transports the carthaginians who fell with them near ecnomus had more judicious arrangement their left wing being about the fourth part the whole their fleet sailed long line along the coast and joining right angle was the main body their large armament which ship ship stood out far into the sea the romans passed the line along the coast and attacked the salient line was not the plan the carthaginian admiral that this should withstand the end the wedge which was forcing itself they therefore set sail and seemed flee separate the romans from their third and fourth lines and the romans pursued them but two parts the long line formed again and fell upon the romans who had detached themselves from the third squadron the third part which was sailing the open sea returned and attacked the fourth roman squadron and the meanwhile the line which was off the coast came and engaged the third squadron which now abandoned the transports their fate thus arose three distinct seafights the first and second roman squadrons conquered easily the fourth
had doubtful victory and the third was hard pressed but the centre turned back defend the boardingbridges were also employed this action with great effect the result was the complete rout the carthaginians thirty ships were sunk part them being driven ashore and wrecked and sixtyfour taken from thirty forty thousand men fell into the power the romans after this defeat the beaten fleet made its escape africa and went protect carthage against attack the men had lost all strength and spirit the romans had the sea clear before them carry their plan into execution and the two consular armies that manlius and that regulus proceeded africa they landed the south side the headland hermum overagainst carthage the mouth the gulf tunis near town which the romans call clupea the greeks aspis the punic name not know place which they took after creditable defence they now made their arsenal and spread from thence into the heart the country the really efficient armies the enemy were stationed sicily the carthaginians had made sure baffling the undertaking and were therefore quite unprepared africa they had fortified colonies the coast only for the interior with the exception few municipia they had the same
policy the vandals who fearing rebellions pulled down all the walls the towns just the lombards afterwards italy wherever therefore the romans came they marched foreign conqueror was looked upon the libyans deliverer for although the carthaginians were barbarians yet they were very hard masters for they followed the system which found throughout the east that the sovereign the owner the soil and the possessor has the enjoyment only long pleases the lord and master they also wanted immense sums money for their celtic and iberian mercenaries and were therefore obliged squeeze them out their subjects the war agathocles the consequences this system had already been seen indeed the spirit the africans had been crushed that they not break out open rebellion they his time for the carthaginians had taken fell revenge after his departure yet they not aid carthage any way most inconceivable order now came from rome that one the consuls manlius should return home being perhaps believed that the force regulus was sufficient itself manlius therefore sailed back with almost the whole the fleet and brought over the booty the carthaginians retreated into inaccessible parts the country regulus nevertheless defeated them near adis their militia troops were
exceedingly timid was easy for the romans drive them out their strongholds regulus stationed himself not far from carthage took the fortified town tunes and encamped near the river bagradas the carthaginians were pressed most closely this camp the ancients generally relate livy also has serpent which was hundred and twenty ells length said have made its appearance and have torn pieces great many romans until the soldiers battered with catapults and ballist this tale the midst account which quite historical most surprising that earth and sea may contain creatures which occur rarely that one inclined take them for fabulous cannot indeed positively denied may have been giant serpent but all likelihood this story like many others has its origin nvius bellum punicum which poet himself served soldier that war all events would wonderful the size the dragon had amounted ells exactly that number which often met with roman measurements namely the carthaginians had utterly lost courage and they could not withdraw their army from sicily without giving that island altogether they therefore sent embassy regulus and sued for peace regulus fame has been very much exaggerated apophthegmatical histories undeservedly represented martyr the heyday his good fortune showed himself ruthless
intoxicated with victory and ungenerous have story him that had then asked the senate for his recall that might attend his farm but know the contrary from polybius that had particularly set his heart upon bringing the war brilliant end before successor arrived much the more senseless was him ask the carthaginians impossibilities and offer them much worse terms than they really obtained the conclusion the war just had meant drive them despair had stipulated for the evacuation sicily and the payment contribution the carthaginians would have been quite willing but had the preposterous idea crushing carthage with one blow his conditions were quite insane even had they been besieged the carthaginians could not have fared worse they were acknowledge the supremacy rome make offensive and defensive alliance with the romans enter into treaty without the permission the romans yield all their ships war but one and have nothing but triremes give sicily sardinia corsica and the lipari isles abandon their italian allies deliver the prisoners and deserters ransom their own captives pay all the expenses the war and contribution besides the carthaginians declared that they would rather perish and luckily for them the romans carried the war badly instead
establishing themselves within the gulf tunis opposite carthage they ought have done they had now sent off their fleet the carthaginians therefore could make use their ships hire troops everywhere among these there were also many from greece one them the celebrated xanthippus who was not diodorus says spartan but learn from polybius neodamode who his education had been subjected the laws the spartans and had thereby acquired inferior right citizenship the case spartan this would have been quite matter course but besides these lacedmonians also and neodamodes even the children foreign might subject themselves the laws lycurgus which position not yet clearly explained xanthippus was one the greatest men his age and furnishes with case point which shows how much sparta must have been stunted owing her not making the lacedmonians equal the spartans came carthage mercenary but officer had certainly been recruiting tnarus when saw the preparations the carthaginians openly declared that was wonder that carthage was going ruin and this was called before the senatein this case was advantage that the military and the administrations were distinctand was asked for his opinion explained them that indeed they had plenty elephants and numidian cavalry which was formidable force
against such small army that the romans the midst enemys country about men according polybius with all the reinforcements perhaps among whom there were cavalry they ought seek the plains whilst the advantage the romans was the mountains the elephants had hardly been employed any battle land all unless perhaps the little skirmish near tunis xanthippus was listened was intrusted with the charge the mercenaries his arrangements excited astonishment the soldiers believed that under his guidance they were sure conquer the whole the camp demanded him for their leader and the carthaginian general who very likely had got his instructions this matter from the city yielded the command him this great resolve when xanthippus had now well drilled the carthaginians went out against the romans into the open field and thereby filled them with great wonder and dismay compelled them fight and made masterly disposition the roman army had centre but the greeks had three divisions and drew his army the following manner the carthaginians occupied the centre phalanx for being townsmen they could only usefully employed masses the two wings placed the mercenaries and joined them the cavalry the flanks the romans likewise put their cavalry the flanks but
placing the infantry they departed from their general custom before the centre the carthaginians hundred elephants had been stationed they formed themselves against these order battle great depth yet the shock was irresistible the left wing the romans indeed conquered the mercenaries but the meanwhile the cavalry the carthaginians had thrown itself upon the right wing and the elephants trampled down everything before them then the phalanx rushed and the whole the roman army was annihilated only two thousand men the left wing made their escape the rear the carthaginians clupea regulus retreated with five hundred romans hill and was obliged surrender xanthippus was now the universal hero they wished him stay carthage but was wise enough return home with the rich presents which received lest should become eyesore envious and heartless people the carthaginians were polybius tells that there was also another account even that the carthaginians had given him bad ship that might perish the passage and that according some had really become victim and according others had saved himself getting into another vessel the romans sent out the fleet which had been still preserved take the garrison the besieged town clupea the carthaginians went against them and
were defeated the number ships which according polybius were captured this occasion very likely have been changed from the romans now evacuated africa taking with them the garrison clupea and they sailed back for syracuse make their passage through the straits messina rome was the time the summersolstice the pilots warned them against the possibility storm the sirocco that season the year sometimes increases into the most dreadful hurricane and the coast those parts destitute harbours but the commanders scorned them most likely because they were foreigners and thus terrible shipwreck between agrigentum and pachynus utterly destroyed nearly three hundred vessels out three hundred and sixty which was the most dreadful disaster that had occurred until then not long afterwards seleucus callinicus also suffered similar shipwreck the carthaginians might now believe that the romans would grant peace fair terms for this reason said they sent regulus rome with offers peace could not get them accepted was obtain least exchange prisoners yet regulus advised against both these things returned carthage and was there put death torture the first who with great independence spirit proved the groundlessness this story was the excellent french philologist paulmier grentemesnil palmerius lived the times the brothers

fleet having had wonderful escape the small syrtis when bound for italy they were again overtaken the passage storm and hardly vessel was saved the southern gales every one them from southeast southwest are always the mediterranean the most dangerous stormwinds and they are the more destructive the italian coast almost without any harbours and full breakers the storms which blow from the north are harmless yet when the currents from the adriatic and the pontus meet ships during north easterly wind are irresistibly drawn into the syrtes from that they are them before their reckonings would lead one suppose this was now second blow for the romans and one from which they not recover they not think making peace yet they tried carry the war less expense the carthaginians were masters the sea and they made use their superiority lay waste the italian coasts but they managed the war wretched manner the romans remained unshaken sicily and thus although indeed they shunned general engagement they took several strong places under the very eyes the enemy and reduced the carthaginians the possession the northwestern part sicily the year according cato fortune turned her back upon the carthaginians ccilius metellus defeated
hasdrubal near palermo hasdrubal had tried take advantage the great fear which the romans had the african cavalry and recover palermo very likely with the connivance the inhabitants encamped its beautiful plain about half german mile from the town and ravaged the fields metellus kept himself his fortified camp ready fight showed himself here great general and made his particular object render the elephants harmless the carthaginians advanced attack the camp metellus drew all his light troops the edge the ditch with good supply missiles the legions manuvred the flanks the light infantry now sallied forth against the enemy enticed them and then threw themselves into the ditch and hurled immense number javelins and burning arrows against the carthaginians and their elephants the campfollowers were constantly bringing them fresh ammunition from the town and the same time the soldiers from behind the breastworks discharged their pila the carthaginians now wished sweep them down with one mighty onset but the elephants were wounded and thus became wild and several them plunged into the trenches from whence the lightarmed soldiers the romans jumped behind the fortified lines and the maddened beasts turned against their own masters this was the moment for which
metellus had waited all along from the sidegates the lines the legions burst forth routed the carthaginian infantry and put their whole army flight more than hundred elephants were captured these were brought rome rafts built for the purpose and killed missiles the circus perhaps give the people representation the battle which they had been taken this victory restored the courage the romans yet the conclusion the war was extremely hard bring about they not again venture over africa and the carthaginians made attempts recover what they had lost sicily the latter were now pent quite the western end the island all that they had still left were the towns lilybum drepana and eryx the year after the romans therefore began the siege lilybum which lasted till the close the war yet not siege form but blockade the part the war which follows might with great propriety called the lilyban one this last act the finest the side the carthaginians the romans distinguish themselves only their perseverance the victory metellus the fourteenth year the war was the first pitched battle with the exception that near adin africa which the romans had conquered the siege lilybum was undertaken them under very
unfavourable circumstances the carthaginians were fact masters the sea but owing the tremendous expenses the war they had retrenched their naval armaments much they possibly could the romans had again fleet off lilybum which was likewise limited force and not intended for seafights yet sufficient make the communication difficult with that town lilybum punic name means according bochart the place which lies towards libya was without doubt mixed punicolibyan colony and that time the only punic town sicily having been founded the inhabitants motye which had been destroyed dionysius lilybum was the residence the carthaginian general had grown into considerable town just carthagena spain palermo the contrary was thoroughly greek city peopled greeks and hellenized siculians and sicanians although had long been under the punic rule lilybum had good harbour which was yet safer from its being difficult get into the sand which the south winds bring thither from the syrtes had already accumulated there and formed sort lagune owing this very cause the whole harbour marsala now longer existence the fortifications the place were very strong besides lilybum three german miles from the carthaginians had drepana the present trapani with its noble harbour which even now spite the attempts
charles fill excellent and besides drepana the town eryx with the mountain that name within this district the war was concentrated for nine years this gave rise the utter wretchedness the island which was quite ruined the romans blockaded lilybum the land side and the same time cruised before the harbour they battered the wall and pulled down part but himilco the commander the carthaginians withstood them with the most unflinching steadfastness disposition treachery often showed itself among the troops the carthaginians for they scarcely ever employed their citizens soldiers but only officers and some also the cavalry the main body therefore consisted mercenaries that the more wondered that the carthaginians had distinguished generals for this reason they had now much trouble secure the attachment these soldiers who were gathered together from all quarters most them being greeks gauls and spaniards they could scarcely manage them any other means than the hope gain hamilcar and hannibal alone knew how bind themselves even these mixed masses their own personal qualities all other times these men were ready commit every sort treachery for money into plot this kind some them now entered with the roman consul but achan alexo discovered and tried

blockading they tried therefore throw mole across the entrance the harbour this however they only succeeded far some measure obstruct the communication the carthaginians with the town which had hitherto been too free the course long war this some distinguished carthaginian generals had already been formed but not single one among the romans whose advantage lay only their troops the romans without the enemys being aware received reinforcements under the command the consul claudius the son claudius ccus who had all the faults his father but none his great qualities was reckless unprincipled man account the great expense rome seems have confined herself one army uncertain whether claudius had already come out consul sicily before the sally himilco only after the roman fleet was lying near lilybum most the vessels being drawn the strand while only single ships rode out sea keep the blockade the sailors had been armed and made fight shore but infectious diseases had broken out some extent might expected the small island sicily being quite exhausted the war many also had perished the engagements that seamen were scarce remedy this defect sailors were enlisted rome they were however people the lowest rank whose property was under

they only offered its people who had reckoned upon having freedom rule which perhaps was still more oppressive than that the carthaginians with whom they had opportunity getting pay these employed mercenaries whilst the romans only occasionally took small bodies celtiberian troops into their service the romans also now revenged themselves some towns which had behaved with particular fury against them there happened this period some horrible events the outbursts fanaticism bravery which turned into madness such was the defence illiturgis and astapa from the latter these all who were able bear arms sallied forth and fought the last man and the same time those who remained behind killed the women and children and set fire the town laying hands themselves also while was burning while scipio was now putting the province order which was still limited catalonia valencia and andalusia insurrection was planned among the spaniards few the spanish states were republics most them were governed princes two whom mandonius and indibilis after long alliance with the romans had imbibed furious hatred against them here also that nationality the spaniards which one meets with all ages displays itself the wrath which all once breaks out against the foreigners whom
they had wished from the beginning only use tools these events are also remarkable for another reason being the first traces state things which long afterwards showed itself more decided shape the tendency the italian allies towards equality with the romans yet our accounts them are incomplete and not hit the main point scipio was very and report got abroad his death time when there was stationed near sucro army eight thousand men consisting italian allies and not livy says romans these resolved make themselves masters spain and found independent state the first pretext this insurrection was the arrears their pay which although was taken from their own treasuries they received much more irregularly than the romans the whole they felt that they were neglected and yet they well knew that there was doing without them they chose two from among themselves umbrian and latin from cales their generals and even invested them with the consular insignia which zonaras mentions though livy says nothing about these took the command and were entering into understanding with the two spanish princes the crisis seemed most highly dangerous but when the tidings scipios recovery reached the camp they once lost courage and his
personal character had such influence that they abandoned every idea insurrection and thought nothing but making their peace scipio came down carthagena behaved deemed them the right and intimated them that they might atone for their offence serving against the spanish princes and that they were carthagena receive their pay either singly body they determined upon coming body this seemed the safer plan and they believed that everything had been forgiven them and their minds were set quite ease when the day before their entry into carthagena they met with quartermaster who told them that the roman army was march catalonia thus they arrived the evening and were quartered the suburbs the officers the town itself the latter were invited the houses the most respectable romans and arrested during the night the next morning the roman army which could implicitly rely made show marching out the gates and the mutineers were summoned the forum get their pay these had their suspicions completely lulled and they came unarmed but the gates the columns were ordered halt they occupied all the streets and hemmed the mutineers scipio now addressed these last and told them what punishment they had deserved yet contented himself
with having only the ringleaders thirtyfive number seized and put death the rest received their pay and were let off after this the war against the spaniards was easy the two princes were pardoned their oath keep quiet before scipio had yet left spain achieved feat romantic daring going over africa visit syphax the king the masssylians who lived eastern and part western algeria and whose capital was cirta the geography those countries the time the carthaginian rule one the most obscure syphax was not tributary the carthaginians but that sort dependence which the prince barbarous people must upon very powerful and civilized state served them for pay and felt altogether subordinate sometimes was quite their disposition others fell away from them after which would make peace again just then was peace with them but had previously when war made overtures the romans and his demand for roman officers train his troops scipio had sent over envoys with full powers this however led results for the meanwhile peace had been concluded and syphax kept neutral scipio now ventured cross over his invitation the hope forming alliance with him had from the very first entertained the just notion attacking carthage her
own ground here actually met with hasdrubal son gisgo the same banquet the object the conduct syphax towards the romans was not allow the carthaginians become too powerful and draw money out them that let scipio escape really wondered spain all was now ended and scipio returned italy where however was not granted triumph because while conducting this war had not held any curule office every other mark honour was shown him was still proconsul before that had been dile had not yet been prtor nevertheless now stood for the consulship though had not yet reached the age prescribed law the leges annales very wise enactment had been set aside for long the war should last was unanimously chosen all the centuries the nation longed see the end the war and every one expected from him far can see this was nothing but one those silly notions which the public are easily taken the great men was said were right glad that the war with hannibal should drag thus they could much the oftener get for themselves the highest dignities scipio who was the idol the people was withstood the party the grandees which fabius deemed the mainspringa party just
like the one which livy describes having existed carthage against hannibal yet one ought fair even that party old fabius maximus perhaps already his eightieth year was its head for more reasons than one perhaps even because like every old man who sees his own brightness fading away was inclined look upon the rising young men with unfavourable eyes scipio also from the very circumstance his being common man may have seemed the romans very incomprehensible character many may have been afraid that his good luck would make him reckless regulus others that might tempt him overthrow the constitution that this suspicion was utterly groundless far was founded upon scipios personal disposition may safely asserted yet find mentioned here and there that was intended make him consul censor for life had this been done would have been king although things then were this could not possibly have been brought about without bloodshed yet shows that the mistrust after all was not without reason hence was that determined opposition manifested itself the senate whose department belonged grants men and money scipio tried get africa for his province but they gave him sicily without allowing him any other troops but those which
were there already however got leave try his chance expedition with those who might voluntarily offer themselves this conduct the senate towards scipio acknowledged fact and rome was very nearly the point losing again all the advantages the war this behaviour the senate ought borne mind when its stedfastness the war with hannibal spoken the influence scipios personal qualities was now seen italy there was famine and disease and yet part the etruscan and umbrian states which were not obliged bear any burthens whatever and therefore owing the regard which the romans then had for every sort privilege had remained full vigour whilst rome had worn herself out exerted themselves for scipio much they had themselves undertake war they built fleet for him and equipped arretium gave him arms for thirty thousand men and likewise money and provisions from the sabines picentines marsians and other neighbouring peoples great number veterans and young discharged soldiers volunteered serve under him thus got considerable fleet and large army quite against the wishes the senate crossed over sicily made from thence attempt upon locri and took that town from hannibal yet the whole the year his consulship passed off without any thing remarkable why
waited long sicily has not been fully accounted for seems that took matters easy and willingly lingered these sicilian regions being particularly delighted with syracuse mens expectations were most signally disappointed had been believed that soon his preparations were all complete would pass over africa and now was understood that was living quite the greek style syracuse commissioners thereupon were sent inquire into the matter and the charge were true depose him but overawed them that they reported that was means wasting his time but was finishing his preparations hannibal after the battle sena had already foreseen the issue the war but not yet lose courage the contrary deemed his duty struggle the last moment that the romans might not sure their own country yet could not defend such extensive provinces evacuated apulia messapia the country the hirpinians and the greater part lucania that only kept the southeastern part and bruttium here remained for three campaigns with perseverance which livy himself admires like lion made whoever dared touch him pay heavily for within this narrow tract country had recruit and provision his army and detain the romans keep them away from africa living the whole time the midst peoples whom
drove despair the most exorbitant demands and succeeded all this without thought either rebellion violence being awakened against him yet was neither able pay nor feed his army and suffered from plague and hunger his headquarters and arsenal was croton thus the war went until the carthaginians called him africa the romans narrowing his district more and more wresting from him one place after the other was not till the year after his consulship when his proconsular imperium was prolonged that scipio with four hundred transports protected forty quinqueremes crossed over africa the carthaginians had had their ships war assembled they must have baffled scipios undertaking but this could hardly have been the case else their inactivity would have been quite unaccountable how many troops carried over was unknown even the ancients themselves average number may assume sixteen thousand men foot several thousand horse and considerable fleet when these departed there were great tremblings heart the timid party among the romans who thought nothing but the fate regulus scipios arrangements were admirable three days made the passage and landed north carthage not far from utica near headland the mouth the river bagradas which like almost all the rivers which fall

himself the expense carthage which was aided the romans but his son who already stood different relation them the third punic war certainly them great deal mischief romance has been got which masinissa love with sophonisbe and therefore jealous syphax with the latter said have been involved war and afterwards reconciled now came would seem ally the carthaginians against scipio who enticed him over had lost his hereditary right owing the carthaginians having favoured rival his for some time had roved the desert now wished try his luck with the romans and showed himself useful them centre round which host africans gathered imparted scipio his plan which had beguiled the carthaginians and scipio fell upon them from ambush the loss was considerable for carthage comprised number her citizens the carthaginian general hanno was taken prisoner and afterwards exchanged for masinissas mother the meanwhile syphax had had the presumption act mediator between the romans and carthaginians which course came nothing everything was then remain before and hannibal and scipio were each them withdraw from italy and africa but the attempt was use scipio for while this was going was able establish himself africa scipio besieged utica with success hasdrubal and syphax
