and summary his history the carthaginians became convinced that their force was not sufficient they had indeed succeeded attempt against the roman ships but this was also the only time during the three years the war africa they sent word hannibal and mago that both them were come which was good news for italy yet was uncertain whether the transport the armies was possible the carthaginians also made scipio proposals peace which listened the more readily had now for three years been proconsul africa and had always expect his dismissal which case the consul the following year claudius nero would have carried away the glory having ended the war moreover the issue the contest with hannibal was still very doubtful and therefore the conditions scipio hard they were were yet tolerable comparison with what happened afterwards the independence the carthaginians was acknowledged they were masters the whole tract country within the punic canal what its extent was uncertain give italy spain sicily and sardinia and likewise all their ships but thirty probably triremes and deliver the prisoners war how much was asked way payment for the expenses the war uncertain livy says that the annalists stated the numbers very differently
the exact numbers which meet with the later greek writers fifteen hundred talents appian are taken from these statements between which livy does not venture decide the latter mentions also great quantity corn these conditions the rulers carthage were resolved make peace but quite different was the feeling the restless unruly populace who fiercely raved against the peace without however being willing shed drop their own blood these were despair after having gloriously fought for long were they was said declare themselves vanquished while hannibal was still alive for the great mass the people certainly looked upon him idol the meanwhile the government carried its point and truce was concluded and ambassadors sent rome there the peace was accepted condition that hannibal should leave italy but the carthaginians now heard that hannibal was really going evacuate italy and they thought that they might try different tack the peace was all but sworn when large roman fleet which had arrived with provisions but had not yet landed them was driven from its moorings storm carthage had for long time been want food and the people murmured this supply being allowed the enemy when the gods themselves were against them and they
could take they liked they embarked riotous manner and cut out the roman ships which relying the truce had cast anchor there scipio this sent envoys remonstrate and demand satisfaction this however was not had such was the general fermentation and the roman emissaries got away with great difficulty was only under the protection guard that they managed return their ship whichcontrary true the wish the governmentwas chased carthaginian vessel and had save itself running ashore this story reminds one the murder the french ambassadors rastadt all hope peace was now utterly gone and the carthaginian ambassadors were commanded withdraw from rome mago had landed from spain genua had taken and was trying change liguria into carthaginian province just the romans had spread spain from one single place yet made but little progress the apennines and the alps had deal with host unmanageable petty tribes although indeed got reinforcements and money his means first were inconsiderable yet always obliged the romans employ some forces against him once defeated them the country the insubrians that had not now been recalled would certainly have given them great deal trouble embarked but died the wounds which had received that engagement hannibal had likewise
had positive orders embark and one cannot understand why the romans not their utmost destroy his fleet reached africa without accident against carthage itself the romans were not able undertake anything was too strong town nor had scipio yet taken any other city that was fortified though was master many open places hannibal landed near adrumetum had taken with him all those whom could find bruttium able bear arms and had embodied among his troops all the roman and italian deserters whose only chance life depended the war with rome his army consisted about forty thousand men yet when beheld the state things carthage made attempt negotiate for saw how unlikely was that the war would successfully carried and knew well that battle were lost the city would obtain peace from which might never recover scipio likewise was very anxious for peace for was always afraid that they would not prolong his imperium the conditions which hannibal offered were too low demanded for the carthaginians the sovereignty over africa leaving indeed the romans the countries which they had conquered but refusing everything else scipio still wished keep the former conditions with trifling compensation for the wrong which had been done
all was spoilt last the folly the carthaginian people who now that hannibal was come thought that scipios army would destroyed like that regulus and thus the famous battle zama was brought hannibal according the testimony polybius here also displayed the qualities great general drew his army three lines the foremost was formed medley foreign troops enlisted from among the most opposite races behind these were placed the carthaginian citizens who only took arms times the utmost need but were forced these very circumstances brave behind these again reserve were the italians whom had brought over and they were considerable body front the whole were eighty elephants and the wings were the cavalry this the only battle which hannibal made use elephants the romans were set their usual array hastati principes and triarii save only that scipio left large spaces between each these three divisions whereas otherwise they were placed behind each other that the maniples the one always covered the intervals between two maniples the others these wide spaces well front the lines put the light troops that when the elephants approached they might hurl their missiles them and then should they enter these open lanes assail them with
javelins the wings set the numidian and roman horse the result the battle shows that this cavalry was now superior quality least that the carthaginians for the latter was soon put flight the object with regard the elephants was partly attained most them ran right through these lanes although there were some who turned themselves sideways upon the men who were armed with javelins now began the shock between the hastati and the carthaginian mercenaries who after gallant fight were forced throw themselves upon the carthaginian phalanx behind them but were driven back again these upon the romans that they were trampled down between the two the hastati however had give way before the carthaginians scipio then made them fall back and the principes and the triarii move sideways towards the wings attack the carthaginians the flank this had the fullest success the italians alone fought with desperate courage but the carthaginian cavalry had been all destroyed and the romans burst upon the carthaginian rear which the rout became such that nearly the whole the army was cut pieces hannibal himself escaped with small handful men adrumetum nothing else was now thought carthage but peace was the great hannibal who
principally negociated and accepted the conditions which course were much harder than the former ones the eagerness however scipio hurry the peace was the saving carthage her independence was acknowledged the towns and provinces which had belonged the carthaginians africa before the war they were indeed still keep subjects but this there was trickery they were prove what they had possessed instead thirty triremes being left them first only ten were now allowed them they had deliver over their elephants and were more tame any they were pay ten thousand euboc talents dollars within fifty years give hundred and fifty hostages chosen the romans themselves which was very hard hostages were badly treated among the ancients and yield all the roman prisoners and deserters and likewise the unfortunate italians who had come over with hannibal whether these were all put death rebels sold for slaves not told livy who indeed says not word about the whole this article appian has given the account and therefore polybius likewise they were moreover acknowledge masinissa king the numidians within the boundaries prescribed the romans conclude passive alliance offensive and defensive with the romans whom however was not binding and feed and keep the
roman soldiers for six months longer africa they might wage war only with the consent the romans out africa not all and they were not enlist mercenaries anywhere europe some fools carthage wanted speak against these conditions but hannibal seized hold one gisgo and dragged him down from the platform which was haranguing outcry was raised about the violation the liberty the citizen hannibal however justified himself saying that ever since his ninth year had been for six and thirty years away from his country and therefore was not accurately acquainted with the law that moreover deemed the peace necessary all men sense had become aware that the peace was now unavoidable and that matters would have taken different turn hannibal had been supported the right time scipio now evacuated africa all the carthaginian ships war were brought sea and there set fire thus ended after sixteen years the second punic war and the rivalry carthage rome had made immense booty the macedonian war immediately after the battle cann philip macedon had sent ambassadors hannibal and had concluded treaty which fell chance into the hands the romans even without this accident could not have been kept secret not least for
any length time this treaty which certainly read polybius genuine text and which the form not all greek but quite foreign undoubtedly carthaginian the two states had not after all bound themselves much hannibal secured philip case victory that the romans were give their possessions beyond the adriatic corcyra apollonia epidamnus the colony pharus the atintanians epirote people dimalus and the parthinian illyrians and return for this philip was let the carthaginians have the supremacy over italy had philip then been what became his riper years this alliance would have proved dangerous the romans but they with that perseverance and heroic courage which distinguished them the whole war sent out fleet under the prtor valerius lvinus protect illyria and raise party against him greece hostilities began the year lvinus not being consul the commencement not quite certain and the war lasted until the peace sempronius this war was carried very sluggishly the side the romans and philip who had limit his exertions only the few points the mainland illyria could have made himself master these had not managed his affairs quite feebly his conduct then gives quite different idea his powers from that which are led form afterwards had given
hannibal but ten thousand macedonians auxiliaries rome would have been sad plight but was too vain philip was that time very young hardly his twentyfirst second year his father demetrius had left him his death yet child and had given him for guardian uncle elder cousin antigonus epitropus likewise called doson this antigonus showed conscientiousness which considering the time which lived really awakens our wonder seems have taken much care the education his ward his rights this see the traces philip especially the first years his reign which said have been very amiable but there was something badhearted him which soon shook off that influence like eastern youth then wallowed lust yet was endowed with remarkable talents was highly gifted general and had courage and skill employ and increase the resources his empire the war against the romans under flamininus displayed much ability and when the peace had lost part his kingdom cleverly took advantage circumstances set again rome herself thus managed leave behind his son power such himself had never possessed before the empire macedon during the latter days antigonus gonatas had fallen into decay the tolians had risen the achans had made themselves free under demetrius was going
down hill still faster from this condition only recovered the last years the guardianship antigonus and that the treason old aratus who sacrificed the whole glory wellspent life for chose rather yield corinth and the liberty greece and make the achans sink into utter insignificance than let cleomenes have that authority the state which was due him and without which the lacedmonians could not have joined the achan league philip the beginning his reign had conjunction with the achans undertaken war against the tolians which the latter were considerably humbled important fortresses thessaly having been taken from them and their estimation greece lowered they were obliged agree disadvantageous peace yet they still kept their independence when philip leagued himself with hannibal and began the war with the romans greece was peace thessaly with the exception that part which was tolian phocis locris euba with chalcis corinth hera and aliphera were well affected macedon and had macedonian garrisons the achans were nominally free and united but reality dependent their allies the macedonians were likewise the botians and acarnanians the tolians who were hostile were free and had territory considerable extent lacedmon that time one revolution followed upon another was subjected nominal
king probably son eudamidas but soon afterwards machanidas seized upon the government the syrian kings ruled over western asia with the exception caria and samos which well the hellespont chersonesus and the towns the southern coast thrace belonged egypt chios lesbos and byzantium formed together confederacy free cities rhodes was free the mistress the sea and powerful she was friend the romans without being actually allied with them egypt and syria were war with each other the former retained clesyria when the peace was made but she lost the northern fortresses phnicia syria the athenians were friendly terms with the romans their enfeebled state they kept aloof from all political activity there was peace everywhere the eyes greece were already very much turned towards rome one would have thought that under these circumstances philip might have undertaken something importance against rome yet not exert himself the beginning the contest there were only little skirmishes going and had some success overcame the atintanians and also the ardyans the north illyricum who were under the protection rome about the fourth year the war the romans made alliance with the tolians and from that time unhappily for greece they became enterprising those parts
they sent over indeed but one legion fact only marines but they also had fleet those seas which was some consequence the macedonians had scarcely any all through the tolians the romans also became connected with attalus who having begun with the small realm pergamus had conquered lydia and created rich principality the roman fleets lvinus and after him sulpicius were real curse for fated greece the treaty with the tolians stipulated that all the places beyond corcyra which they should conquer together the soil should belong the tolians the inhabitants with their goods and chattels the romans such stipulation indeed not unheard yet shows what the tolians really were after the lamian war they deserve praise but all that happened afterwards shows them have been morally barbarians their language may indeed have been partly greek this treaty had the saddest consequences the roman fleet made its appearance off the greek coast gina dyme oreus were taken and the whole population swept away the romans these two last places the tolians were not able keep but gina with its harbour they sold attalus for thirty talentsthat noble greek island prince pergamus these atrocities drew upon the tolians and romans the
abhorrence the whole greece philip who thereby became popular penetrated with the greeks for the first time into tolia and requited them their own country for their devastations the tolians abandoned the romans concluded very disadvantageous peace philip made considerable conquests two three years afterwards livys chronology here very little relied about the romans also means tib sempronius concluded peace with philip beneath the conditions which some great disadvantage again veiled not only the country the atintanians which had become subject thema district not unimportant itself but very great consequence account the pass argyrocastro through which philip had now free passage between the roman territory and the then republic epiruswas expressly ceded philip but also the country the ardyans the romans course had this mental reservation that the time would not long before they would break this peace and gain back what they had lost this one the few instances which the romans renounced part their possessions one ought have remembered this when such violent reproaches were made against jovian who save his army ceded tract country the persians there was outcry the time such thing had never happened before the history rome aurelian had yielded dacia the goths hadrian
had given the conquests trajan the east not mention the peace with the volscians the earliest times philip after having concluded peace with the romans allied himself with antiochus the great against the infant ptolemy epiphanes the child the unworthy ptolemy philopator the egyptian kings since philadelphus and euergetes were possession extensive districts and strongholds the coasts syria and asia minor far the coast thrace lycia least was subject their supremacy under ptolemy philopator the empire had already fallen into utter decay and his infant successor was growing under the charge unworthy guardian antiochus and philip took advantage the moment egypt had since the rise the alexandrine empire been friendly terms with rhodes and the rhodians had strong interest being friends with alexandria they had much more fear from macedon than from egypt they therefore defended epiphanes yet their power was match for that macedon and syria especially the wretched egyptian government hardly anything but the contrary let the allies among whom besides rhodes there were also byzantium chios and attalus pergamus bear the whole brunt the war the two kings were therefore most successful philip conquered for himself the whole the thracian coast perinthus ephesus and lycia fell the
lot syria although the allies the egyptians had shortly before had some success seafight near chios philip had now reached the pinnacle his greatness even from crete where macedon had never before exercised any influence was applied for his mediation the immediate cause least the pretext for the second macedonian war was afforded the romans the distress athens that city was utterly impoverished and decayed but kept sort independence and early about twentyfive years after the first illyrian war had made alliance with the romans and had granted them isopolity perhaps the romans received the gift with smile yet such bright rays her old departed glory still lingered upon athens that her side least there was nothing ridiculous the proffer pausanias tells that among the cenotaphs for those who had been slain there were also some for the men belonging three triremes who had fallen battle abroad allies the romans but does not give the date not likely that this was figment the athenians the time may have been that the second illyrian war they were keen enough see that they might gain the romans sending them few ships during the first macedonian war they very wisely kept neutral but
the last years the war hannibal they got involved hostilities with philip the murder two young acarnanians who had intruded when the eleusinian mysteries were celebrated led their countrymen call upon philip for help had long wished get possession athens and now savagely devastated the whole attica the very walls the city all the temples the athenian territory were pulled down and even the tombs were demolished the athenians betook themselves the rhodians attalus and general all the allies that suddenly decayed alexandrine empire which had once been highly blooming under euergetes yet their hopes were chiefly bent upon the romans rome there was much consultation what the senate and the leading men who already had unbounded views extending the roman power would not have hesitated for moment declare war and the more they were likewise eager make for what they had lost the unfortunate issue the former one but the people who were most wretchedly off and longed for rest threw out the first motion for war most erroneous thing for one believe that constitution remains the same long its outward forms still last when alterations have taken place the distribution property public opinion and the way which people
live the constitution even without any outward change may become quite different from what was and the selfsame form may one time democratical and another aristocratical this internal revolution hardly ever traced modern writers history and yet one those very things which history ought particularly searched into that strange and wonderful preponderance the oligarchy wealth existed already that time rome and the manywho generally speaking have neither judgment nor will their ownnow decree the very things which they not wish here indeed have one the first and most remarkable symptoms this the people contrary their own wishes vote for the war with philip was the great misfortune rome that after the war hannibal there was great man who had the genius restore the constitution accordance with its spirit for great states always decline and fall because after great exertions everything left the blind spirit the age and healing what diseased attempted the romans now with great zeal sent ambassadors philip demand indemnification for the athenians and cessation all hostilities against the allies rome the number whom ptolemy also belonged philip clearly saw that this was but pretext raise quarrel and had bitterly repent not having taken better advantage the war
with hannibal the year the war was decreed and the command was given the consul sulpicius galba who had already made campaign before those parts though not the most glorious kind devastated dyme oreus and gina must have been resolved upon late the season and the consul besides fell nothing more could undertaken that year galbas expedition therefore entirely belongs the year which followed his consulship fact which overlooked livy villius the next consul was only present the seat war for very short period towards the end his time office greece the tolians just then were very much weakened but independent and hostile macedon they possessed tolia part acarnania the country the nianians that the ozolian locrians most phthiotis the land the dolopians part southern thessaly and thermopyl and they had isopolity with lacedmon and with number distant places elis and messene yet for the last thirty years they had been going down hill the peloponnesus the achans held achaia sicyon phlius and argolis and arcadia but reality they were entirely dependent the macedonians and were protected them against tolia and lacedmon the lacedmonians were confined within very narrow limits their old country and they had lost their ancient constitution
they had ephors perhaps not even senate but they were ruled tyrant nabis one the worst monsters the messenians stood apart from the tolians and achans and were become sworn foes the latter the eleans were independent and leagued with the tolians the botians remained independent appearance only under the supremacy macedon corinth euba phocis locris were nominally allies the macedonians but fact were subject their rule thessaly was held state which had become blended with macedon epirus the house the acid was extirpated and the remainder the people hemmed the tolians formed republic sometimes under tolian and other times under macedonian influence the greek mainland athens survived mere name without connexion belonging her object philips hate the acarnanians were properly speaking none the subjects the macedonians but were only united with them their common enmity against the tolians the cyclades had formerly belonged egypt and they were now unsettled state crete was independent but torn factions owing which philip had been called upon mediate chios and mitylene were free rhodes was great and powerful byzantium also was free and allied with chios and mitylene they had taken little part possible all the quarrels but now they were drawn into
them particularly chios and league with attalus their intellectual life the greeks were utterly fallen there were indeed still some schools athens but poesy was dead and even the art speech that last blossom the greek spirit had vanished away and had sought new home among the asiatic peoples which had been hellenized but without imbibing any the excellencies the greek nation most places were mere shadows what they had been there were but few indeed which had not been destroyed more than once the number those spared was corinth which therefore was the most flourishing all greek towns the achans ever since aratus out spite the lacedmonians had given over his country into the hands the macedonians were mere clients their new patrons owing this connexion which had lasted nearly twenty years they had many time received the deepest cause for provocation but they were bad terms with their neighbours and their patriots had any wish was have their dependence upon macedon changed into freer form clientship none however dreamed independence but then many were filled with bitter indignation the cruelty with which several towns had been laid waste the romans the tolians felt inclined undertake the war but
they not come any decision misunderstanding having arisen between them and the romans whom they reproached with having given them unfounded hopes whilst the other hand the romans complained not having been supported them the illyrian war the first campaign sulpicius the romans could nothing they took the bull the horns and attacked macedon from illyria philip kept the defensive that part illyria far scutari country rather low hills very much like franconia many places flat the eastern frontier near macedon ridge high mountains runs down which takes western macedon and from scodrus scardus reaches southwards pindus and parnassus this range mountains lofty and broad cold barren and naturally poor now hardly inhabited any longer even the valleys are inhospitable here are the highlands macedon the true home the earliest macedonians who had formerly held under their own liegelords being dependent upon philip but that time were entirely united with macedon the romans found every thing here against them nearly the whole the population consisting macedonians was hostile with the exception the epirote orestians and provisions were scarce everywhere sulpicius therefore retreated and passed the winter the fertile country lower illyria near apollonia and epidamnus however carefully historians may disguise
the fact certain that his undertaking was complete failure quinctius flamininus immediately after his being made consul the year led reinforcements across the adriatic and changed the whole plan this time also the macedonians had fortified their frontiers and they kept the defensive the principal camp the king was near what now argyrocastro the old antigonea founded pyrrhus where the aousso must read instead apsus plutarchs life flamininushas worn its way between two high ridges limestone both these mountain ranges are wild and impassable they stretch out one side far the acroceraunian heights the other towards pindus the place cannot mistaken from its very nature fauces antigone even this day the true road from illyria into the interior epirus passes through part which the brink the river cut the mountains the romans had renewed their alliance with the tolians who took arms and threatened the frontier thessaly but undertook nothing consequence philip was much bent hindering the tolians now that they were the allies the romans from attacking the thessalian frontiers right earnest and uniting with them and this effected taking his position near antigonea before this defile villius also who when flamininus arrived was still greece had during his
proconsulship stood his ground against philip yet was hopeless attack him front and several attempts had miscarried perhaps the romans expected that the tolians would compel the macedonian army change their position otherwise would incomprehensible why they should have encamped that place flamininus who now entered upon the consulship was distinguished man and had moreover been chosen the people before was thirty years old owing their confidence his personal qualities indeed proof the utter falsehood the notion that the romans had only later times sought make themselves acquainted with greek literature when find distinctly stated men like flamininus that they were imbued with greek learning his conduct towards greece not indeed approved every respect but was provoked when his noble attempt win her applause was darkened the ingratitude nation which was already partly degenerated had the greeks been able suit themselves the actual state things they might have been spared many sad experience flamininus became convinced that was necessary try and drive the macedonians from their vantage ground and attained his end means that faithlessness then general greece tampered with chieftain belonging the epirote republic the name charops and the latter being gained over money and promises undertook lead small
roman division four thousand men through unknown roads the rear the macedonian army the romans not indeed trust their guides and they carried them bound along with them but treachery was committed and the third day they reached the heights above the macedonians that day had been appointed for the attack sunrise flamininus began the battle front and thus engaged the attention the macedonians had already lost great many men when the detachment which had gone round the macedonians gave the signal with fire from the heights now renewed the attack with redoubled vigour the other romans fell upon the macedonians from the rear and these were panicstruck and fled that the romans one blow became masters epirus where all the towns opened their gates them philip escaped across mount pindus into thessaly flamininus not follow wished first take advantage these circumstances entirely drive the macedonians out greece but expedition thessaly had great results united with the tolians ambracia and took his winterquarters phocis where besieged the strong town elatea during the campaign the combined fleet attalus the rhodians and the romans was the greek seas they made several undertakings which however led nothing but the ravaging unhappy greece thus
chalcis once flourishing was destroyed and pillaged the achans had before been obliged give megara and corinth philip who had likewise kept orchomenus without asking their leave later period only that say the beginning the second war gave back them had now after his defeat likewise restored them corinth they would hardly have forsaken him for they had implacable hatred against the tolians and also against the romans account the savage devastations the former war but now that philip had not been able stand his ground and all the country far thermopyl was the hands the romans the macedonian party although certainly still considerable could not come forward and the proposal was discussed concluding alliance with the romans roman ambassadors appeared sicyon the achan strategus aristnus shrewd statesman took advantage the disposition which was felt many yield sense and reason and dwell the injuries suffered from philip and got the alliance with him dissolved though not without difficulty and another one concluded with the romans the restoration the places which philip had stripped them was promised nabis and the tolians were not exercise any hostility against them was longer possible demosthenes once had done lead the nation inspired eloquence and
high feeling but shrewdness had its effect the achans were not warlike although philopmen had done everything could make them the war with macedon was very irksome them for although there was only small macedonian garrison stationed corinth yet was able its allies much harm the neighbouring places the peloponnesus the governor corinth philocles even took argos the meanwhile flamininus called upon the botians enter into the league with rome yet they showed themselves wavering after hundred and forty years the macedonian yoke seemed impossible that that power should have been suddenly broken was only what was almost stratagem that flamininus managed bring them that alliance the proconsul flamininus consular year had expired but his imperium had been prolonged appeared before thebes and demanded let that might negotiate now had brought soldiers with him who came forward whilst was before the town and marched without asking leave the decree which the botians still made was now but mere form there was however also macedonian garrison the place one hundred and twentyfive years had passed away since the death alexander the proud waves had gone down and the greeks longer deemed themselves the people which alone had been called rule the
world they longer thought macedonians upstarts but they beheld them their protectors against the gauls scordiscans thracians and other northern peoples they looked the macedonian court macedonian money also its work short they acknowledged their leadership nor they indeed any more reckon them barbarians pella greek was doubt much spoken macedonian court and among all the educated classes was the language vogue that the difference between hellenes and macedonians had this time been effaced before the new campaign had begun but when the achans had already declared against him philip sought negotiate would not however yield the demand the romans that should evacuate the whole greece and determined again try his luck war had become much more spirited the course his reign these negotiations failed and the hostile armies marched against each other the year thessaly was the natural scene the campaign this year which philip had put forth all his strength what livy tells his levy true and was indeed able raise but small army then must the gauls have dreadfully visited his country but the statement does not seem correct for macedon had any thing population must easily have furnished hundred thousand men the romans took the field
reinforced the tolians other allies are spoken and the tolians themselves are said not have been more than few thousand foot and four five hundred horse unless this another mistake altogether are told the army flamininus consisted twentysix thousand men and small body horse the struggle began rather early the year the harvest thessaly gathered about the middle june and that time the battle cynoscephal must have taken place for the corn was ripe but not yet cut that the soldiers when foraging had only reap the romans and macedonians who were each advancing fell with each other spot where they were separated only range low hills this was the borders the thessalian plain which the phthiotic hills gently slope away into thessaly proper here the two armies were marching the same direction without knowing each believing the other far behind the object both sides was take their quarters wherever they might find provisions and they wished avail themselves the ripe corn both were their way scotussa had rained the day before and the morning there arose thick fog that they scarcely saw the hills along which they were marching the right and left and the romans chanced hit upon
one which the macedonians were about ascend philip had wish whatever fight the roman general also would rather have chosen another battlefield the country thereabouts was still too open the force circumstances however compelled them engage the romans were already the height when the macedonians came but their number was small and first they were driven back until they got reinforced this took place the left the macedonian army and thus both generals became aware the nearness the enemy and quickly sent troops the help their own men with the support the tolians the romans gained the upperhand the hill but this led the foe make grand attack upon them and they were pushed down again the whole the macedonian left wing the macedonians now thought themselves sure victory and philip was obliged risk battle lest should damp the spirit his soldiers therefore had only choose the best line for their advance and what was bad for the macedonian phalanx had take his position the hill where the moveable array the romans was much more efficient the description this battle polybius fragments masterly the whole the left wing had pressed forward and had driven the romans down the hill the
other side but when the right wing had with great exertion ascended thither the roman left wing was already there before and thus was this part the macedonian army soon defeated the tolian cavalry whom this success was owing went pursuit the fugitives the left wing the romans which had encounter the phalanx the struggle was undecided first they had even the worst the phalanx which was once sixteen deep and now fourteen charged heavily with its immense masses and its terrible sariss the rear ranks pushing those front with almost irresistible force against the enemy but the romans wheeled half round the right and drove the macedonians the other side the heights from which they had come down and this position which the phalanx was not able move the battle was won there denying that the romans owed their victory mainly the tolian cavalry the rout the phalanx was the work these alone philip had narrow escape the macedonians lifted their lances token submission but the romans who not understand this signal fell upon them and thus most them were killed and the rest taken prisoners after this overthrow which the loss the macedonians according the lowest estimates those
which polybius gives was eight thousand killed and five thousand prisoners philip fled larissa and from thence tempe had led the whole his forces into the field that had reserve left this was his fatal mistake therefore began negotiate and after two vain attempts truce was agreed upon was send ambassadors rome and the meanwhile furnish supplies the roman army and pay contribution the romans were inclined peace there had begun much blood between them and the tolians these had plundered the macedonian camp after the battle cynoscephal and consequence dissension had arisen the romans were much greater numbers that fight than the tolians but the cavalry the tolians had indeed decided the victory and moreover the beginning these had stood the brunt the battle the heights which the romans were enabled make orderly retreat there was blinking these arguments the tolians even they had not been vain people might very well have taken themselves the honour the victory and this indeed they way which gave great offence the sensitive flamininus who therefore immediately after the day was won tried cut them out all its advantages throughout the whole greece the tolians were sung conquerors and the romans with their
