with peculiar difficulty owing hamilcar enterprising carthaginian who had remained behind from magos army and had organised the ligurian and gallic forces the insubrians were very different from the boians the former made their submission after one two campaigns but the war with the latter lasted the tenth year they defended themselves with distinguished bravery and they destroyed the fortresses placentia and cremona for they knew that the romans were carrying against them war extermination and they therefore fought with all the energy despair historians not state explicitly fragment cato does that they were utterly rooted out the fate this people remarkable after their emigration from gaul they had either turned themselves italy had gone the danube gaul their seats are now hardly known the country near the danube they were probably exterminated the cimbric war and hence the desertum boiorum bheim bohemia which was afterwards occupied the marcomanni italy they are said have had hundred and twelve cantons that italy they were extirpated and that there could therefore have been question about them was not all understood the jurists who have written the lex gallia cisalpina but all the celts south the were destroyed and the whole their land
taken roman colonies bologna modena parma and also lucca were founded that time and received considerable territory yet even the days polybius that country was nearly without inhabitants and was repeopled only slow degrees the lex julia united the cispadana political rights with italy the close the war with philip the tolians were filled with the most envenomed resentment this bitterness feeling was means softened down the course time for the tolians made too great pretensions and the romans were unfair towards them yet even without that they would have moved heaven and earth drive the romans out greece they therefore turned their eyes towards antiochus antiochus one those princes who unjustly bear history the surname the great the seleucid were poorer great men than any the dynasties which succeeded alexander even seleucus himself hardly deserved called the asiatic degeneracy shows itself them much earlier than among the ptolemies antiochus got that surname because his reign was happy compared with the princes his house who had the same name antiochus soter and the utterly infamous theos his grandfather and greatgrandfather may have been the better man certainly restored his empire which had come him almost state dissolution from his brother
seleucus but this without any grand achievement his own only put forth against his cowardly enemies the comparatively great might his dominion had real difficulties his way and those which had face not overcome like great man might have called himself for before his war with the romans had more extensive monarchy than the kings syria had ever possessed ruled from the hellespont the borders india over phrygia cilicia syria palstine clesyria mesopotamia kurdistan media persia far sidgistan and cabool had made treaties with indian princes and his riches were immense but with all this there was nowhere the vigour warlike state but asiatic effeminacy throughout his strength had not been put the proof the descendants the macedonians and greeks the colonies alexander and seleucus had become quite unwarlike just the pullani the offspring the crusaders the holy land set people with all the vices the east without its virtues yet possessed the whole extent the persian empire antiochus was looked upon asia the and europe the terrible adversary the romans the tolians therefore built great hopes him was natural that hannibal should turn himself towards this prince and try stir him war against rome although things then were not
wish begin once especially had the prospect still remaining for long time the prime life the romans had since the war with philip entered into negotiations with antiochus which however led nothing was step such they had often taken before they would risk enterprise and not mind miscarried when leagued with philip antiochus had gained the egyptian possessions asia minor and dreamt nothing less than extending his empire europe philip consequence his peace with the romans had been obliged abandon the towns which had conquered from the egyptians these were exposed the inroads the savage thracian tribes and they called upon antiochus for help this prince also meddled the feuds the chersonesus and restored lysimachia which had been destroyed the thracians but the romans forbade him set his foot europe they declared that they would never let him overstep the natural boundaries his empire which they very wisely kept this undefined expression was also acknowledge the independence the greek towns asiathis was piece immense presumption put forth those who wanted war antiochus refused and thus the negotiations were carried for four years during which fortified lysimachia and the chersonesus the outworks asia also fitted out fleet for which possessed the
most ample resources having taken the phnician coast from the gyptians and being likewise master cilicia and pamphylia greece the tolians were his side but the rhodians were decidedly against him they were allies the egyptians and though not actually leagued with the romans yet terms such good understanding with them that came nearly the same thing antiochus had not always his abode antioch had that time chosen the beautiful city ephesus for his capital thither hannibal came and was received with the greatest distinction the latter who had passed the first years after the conclusion the second punic war his native city had means given himself despair soon showed himself after the peace great during the war had been made suffete term which also find the book judges meaning the head the state peace and though this was dignity which had not any longer much weight the ruling power carthage was already seriously paralysed the democratical element while office his ability had given its former influence reformed abuses every kind and turned his attention particularly the finances which had found out immense deficit the great men had helped themselves all the good things short brought with him new life
and new hopes into his native city but the more laid abuses bare the faster grew the party the traitors who that time were met with carthage well all the statesa set men who sought their own individual power whilst sacrificing their country the romans the latter who use livys fine expression had made peace with carthage but not with hannibal looked upon him with great mistrust which was very natural his only thought was raise his country rome had long ceased conscientious state her unsullied moral purity which her earlier days was far from being mere dream was quite gone and just when she had the power and therefore the opportunity acting uprightly she broke all the laws honour and virtue the romans had already more than once complained hannibal and now they regularly charged him with the design preparing war and demanded that should given them this embassy however was not set foot without the strongest opposition from the great scipio who denounced such conduct unworthy shameful indeed but before the carthaginians had come resolution which would perhaps have been wrung from them hannibal fled antiochus the king syria hannibal was startled when saw the state the syrian
troops found host which the great mass were barbarians which though apparently trained some measure the macedonian way fighting was unsound the core and quite cowardly under the persian rule was only from single divisions such army that could expect anything but his plan was worthy him advised antiochus bestow his greatest exertions the fleet and means carry the war into italy the picked troops and those which himself still hoped train might then embarked and landed southern italy which was exasperated against rome account the revenge which she had taken greece should not touch for that would irritate philip whom should rather leave and seek aggrandize himself egypt but was natural that men small minds should reject this plan and was resolved transfer the war greece where the tolians were their allies and try and gain over philip the latter plan was the more hazardous and fact quite impracticable owing the folly which the advisers antiochus displayed all that they they wished work upon philip not fair means only but also fear thus the very moment when everything turned upon philips goodwill being won pretender who gave himself out descendant alexander the great and who had been with the
acarnanians epirus was received ephesus the rightful sovereign macedon they even fostered the fond hope bringing about revolution there this was childish folly matters now stood hannibal gave his advice against war and this was accounted him treachery and the wretched king with his wretched councillors thoroughly misunderstood this great man think him capable playing into the hands rome this belief they were confirmed stratagem the romans which bad men only could have been taken scipio was sent over asia for last negotiation with antiochus and hannibal were personally acquainted and two such great men passed lightly over the circumstance their having faced each other enemies they were not mere tools the state but they were two great moral powers arrayed against each other which after mighty struggle had made peace and not ordinary men such cases there kindled truly great souls mutual love they met familiarly and hannibal was thus led offer hospitality scipio which the latter said that would have accepted had not hannibal been dependent enemy rome scipio was perhaps less frank this conversation than hannibal and may have taken advantage him this may have contributed make hannibal suspected when became known that the romans began arm
the tolians demanded that antiochus should come over with his forces greece hannibal saw that antiochus was running his destruction undertook the war with his present means and told him that must gain over philip and possible the egyptians yet there were great difficulties the way these alliances philip united with the tolians the achans were thrown into the arms the romans philip also was angry because antiochus had not supported him his war and moreover should everything turn out most favourably the object antiochus was other than conquer greece therefore became possible weaken rome the macedonians thereby merely got another dangerous neighbour thus the negotiations not advance matters and antiochus had been wise would not have listened the blind rage the tolians and would have been aware their insignificance but thought them great nation the preparations were made with little method that antiochus had more than ten thousand men ready embark the tolians who expected innumerable army had likewise described their own power much larger than really was that was highly astonished find that they had scarcely four thousand men landed demetrias which shall see was already evacuated the romans and now occupied the tolians now reduced phthiotis and
passed over euba and made himself master the strong town chalcis was fated that the romans should justified their unwillingness intrust their fortresses the greeks who not know how behave from thence went botia where was joyfully welcomed phocis and into thessaly this last country had been converted the romans into republic yet had never known how govern itself and owing its having been long dependent macedon had become quite unable take care its own affairs the magnesians and phthiotes had been detached and formed into independent state met with good reception both sides mount and here made fresh acquisitions this was the critical moment had philip energetically declared himself the romans would have been driven back far illyricum but philip was diverted from the romans saw that the war had been begun with little judgment that there was not much expected from moreover had not himself acquired strength enough and knew well that the issue were unfavourable should fare the worst and were wait awhile might hope that the romans would crush his enemies the tolians whilst his position would none the worse and then might quietly abide his time when the greeks would begin hostile the romans therefore
only took possession the town demetrias one the three chief strongholds greece which gave him the command thessaly there must have been secret treaty about with the romans for henceforth remained macedonian until the fall that empire without its evacuation having been called for the district magnesia was also incorporated with macedon the war nabis already bitterness feeling between the romans and achans had begun show itself the latter were mistrustful because the romans had not yet withdrawn their garrisons from the acrocorinth chalcis and demetrias but antiochus was approaching whose power quite exaggerated opinion was entertained the romans were wise enough now remove those garrisons the other greek states likewise fell off one one from rome and there was everywhere roman and macedonian party flamininus now sullied his fair fame allowing the faction devoted himself and the romans botia murder the leader the macedonian faction and screening the guilty from justice the achans were still his friends but very negative ones they not wish join themselves with the tolians antiochus and the tolians had now both sides their eyes opened with regard the expectations which they had entertained each other hannibal who from the very first had been prophet
evil was now called this the usual fate great men long one doing well and one can still follow their advice they are not listened but one has got into trouble acting against then are they charged with obstinacy they declare that nothing any more done hannibal could only propose that they should renew the attempts gain over philip but the latter had already concluded his alliance with rome hoping thereby regain thessaly the same time him the thought was delightful revenging himself the tolians means union with the romans antiochus now ventured more any greater undertaking but the advice his courtiers sought employ the winter making preparations asia this however was only done small extent and the meanwhile wasted his time feasts chalcis the beginning spring new consular army under acilius glabrio which was reinforced the macedonians appeared thessaly where was opposed more than ten thousand asiatics and few tolians and encamped near heraclea whilst antiochus occupied thermopyl just the reverse what happened the days the persians for this time was the asiatics though indeed these were halfmacedonians who their turn defended the pass the achans had now again decidedly joined the romans and they them good service that
the pass thermopyl could turned unless over which there lay path were occupied well was then generally known already experience had twice shown the order take two mountains which covered the defile was given old cato and his friend valerius flaccus the latter was unsuccessful but the former got possession the heights and dashed into the enemys camp along with the flying tolians whilst acilius beat the syrians front the army antiochus broke and was scattered himself escaped chalcis where short time before had been revelling asiatic luxury and childish festivities that town abandoned leaving behind weak garrison which made stand against the romans who however not pursue him and went asia his fleet also the sight roman one which had now arrived sheered off asia minor antiochus looked upon the war ended yet gathered together new army and again gave himself his pleasures there doubt but that would have agreed any peace however indifferent might have been acilius glabrio now turned the war against the tolians heraclea and lamia the thessalian side thermopyl belonged tolia epictetus the former these was besieged the consul lamia philip the siege heraclea where the main force the tolians lay was carried with the
utmost spirit according all the rules military art the town was taken storm and the garrison surrendered discretion the tolians now lost courage yet they were still saved the eagerness the romans pass over into the rich country asia and have done with this toilsome mountain war against race which had nothing and also the anxiety these that philip should not gain his ends when lamia was about fall although without doubt possession had been promised philip the consul sent him word that had made convention for lamia and that therefore the king was give the siege hereupon philip took further share the war beyond reducing the athamanians and the dolopians the tolians would have been extirpated had not the romans themselves wished have them preserved the latter besieged naupactus had they urged this siege with true vigour and earnestness the town must have yielded but they went work sluggishly and with much forbearance which enabled the tolians save the place the war ended with the siege ambracia which that time was tolian and the defence which the little people the tolians though abandoned all the greeks and without any great man head them displayed the highest gallantry the siege
one the most scientific the whole ancient history the description delightful owing the cleverness invention and the stedfastness the besieged does one good see physical weakness holding its own means skill this defence does honour the tolians whose wars are otherwise not very glorious somewhat later date length peace was mediated the athenians the tolians had pay few hundred talents warcontribution acknowledge the supremacy rome and bind themselves follow the romans their wars evacuate ambracia and give them well cephallenia which was taken and laid waste the conquerors like fate had already befallen the acarnanians the peace was hard one yet under the circumstances fair enough thus the romans gained possession the country along the coast and the landing places greece antiochus now confined himself holding out with his fleet against the rhodians and the ships eumenes amongst which there were only very few roman ones unimportant battle was fought which these had the best but after the fleets had separated the rhodians were shamefully deceived surprised and defeated the syrians the roman admiral milius regillus now came with new fleet not more than eighty ships the romans were little made for the seaservice that they kept fleet whatever when
they not actually want one hence likewise least one half their crews were then rhodians for these were the best seamen the age being yet their prime the best days greece the fleet antiochus had been furnished almost entirely the phnician towns which however important they were during the persian rule must now have very much gone down and was commanded hannibal yet though led hannibal was not able effect junction with another division when battle was fought near myonnesus the victory was altogether the side the romans and their allies the fleet antiochus was all but destroyed the ships which were left fled away into two harbours caria this success had been achieved the rhodians was won however means fire the rhodians having engines board their ships which hurled fire upon the enemy most likely kind what was afterwards called greek fire was not thrown with rockets and from the way which historians speak this least certain that the masses were quite extraordinary and that could not quenched this naval victory decided the war antiochus the advice hannibal had meant occupy the chersonesus which joined thrace only narrow tongue land about half mile length this lay lysimachia well fortified
town from whence strong walls stretched out the melas colpos and the propontis that the landside could only taken siege one could land indeed several places but the syrian fleet might have prevented and ought have done would then have been unassailable asia long chose keep the defensive yet such was the blindness this king that sent hannibal hateful reminder rejected counsels pamphylia and banished him from his presence possible that antiochus occupying the chersonesus might have protected asia although could not have kept the long run but what was senseless was his giving without making even much attempt defend the rich magazines there which had been laid for long campaign were abandoned the romans and the garrisons withdrawn from the towns beguiled himself his subjects with the thought that should able make stand behind the hellespont yet this coast also forsook the approach the romans and fell back into lydia the same way the troops philip which even before alexanders days had set foot those shores were not hindered the persians from crossing the year scipio and llius were consuls they both them wished for the command the expedition asia and the senate gave scipio who would not however
have gotten had not his great brother offered serve legate under him for the latter could not appointed consul the law which ten years were elapse between two consulships the same individual was now very strictly adhered scipio had the meantime been censor and his influence was still almost unbounded was plainly shown this occasion when scipio most insignificant being was chosen merely for the sake his brother just the great fabius maximus former times had procured the consulship for his son under whom then acted legate the roman fleet had scarcely appeared off the coast asia the scipios being still macedonia when ambassadors arrived from antiochus ask for the conditions peace offered give the chersonesus acknowledge the freedom the asiatic towns smyrna and abydos which had been taken the romans and bear half the expenses the war these conditions coming from one who owned himself vanquished the romans not accept scipio declared that they would have been good enough before antiochus had evacuated the chersonesus but that now the bridle was put upon asia they marched through macedon and thrace over very difficult roads aided however philip whom they rewarded giving him the possession the towns the thracian coast
when the romans had now crossed the hellespont scipio fell sick thing which often happened him and was not able follow the army was obliged stay behind ela olian town this put stop all the operations and antiochus took advantage the delay set foot fresh negotiations which however led nothing scipio proposed very fair terms but they offended the pride antiochus son the great scipio had some way other been taken prisoner asia and was treated with the greatest distinction the ambassadors first offered set him free then antiochus sent him back without ransom hoping that would now easier for him obtain peace scipio wished that decisive battle might put off until his recovery antiochus the other hand was hurry have fought the armies encountered the borders lydia near magnesia the foot mount sipylus country moderately high hills which one the finest the world being like all the lands along the coast asia minor quite contrast the inland regions which are barren and devastated volcanic convulsions the army antiochus consisted eighty thousand men its chief strength being the macedonian phalanx which all likelihood was made men all countries there were likewise some macedonians among these the descendants the troops alexander
who however were already mingled blood with the asiatic population besides these had peltasts armed the greek manner and host asiatics concerning whose arms and equipments livy and appian tell nothing the romans had only consular army the other was still fighting against the tolians besides two legions and the proportionate number allies there were few thousand achans and small number auxiliaries from eumenes who only ruled over pergamus and some ionian and mysian towns the whole being much less than thirty thousand men they had been advancing against each other for three days the fourth the battle came the large army antiochus outflanked the romans their left wing rested river which however had depth and thus they were outflanked the opposite bank the syrian army consisted the phalanx medley troops attached cavalry elephants and warchariots the romans also had elephants but african ones which they not use because they were far weaker and much more timid than those india the battle was decided the very first onset the victory being contested for moment only the mass the macedonian phalanx and one single point another antiochus drove the roman troops back far their own camp whereupon however was repulsed good
general might with the aid the phalanx have given the romans great deal trouble was still done cynoscephal but all was lost the kings wretched tactics the phalanx first was formed into number smaller bodies with intervals and instead their keeping that order and acting together masses these gathered from fear into one huge cluster which could have been use only plain and extreme danger but here uneven ground there arose immense confusion which the light troops the romans harassed them with their javelins and slings that they all broke and fled just vain had been the attempt the beginning the battle use the scythed chariots against the romans whose skirmishers put them flight the horses were soon made shy this asiatic invention but also found among the celts especially britain the overthrow was complete that was impossible bring together again the small remnants the army the king fled through phrygia and sent xeuxis his ambassador scipio beg for peace stooping the same time the meanest offers scipio was glad come terms possible that scipio received also some presents which was the charge afterwards brought against him yet there need for supposing this roman consul could not have wished for
anything better than make peace before the coming his successor the conditions were followsantiochus was once pay down five hundred talents dollars for the truce the definitive peace was settled rome and soon was concluded was again pay two thousand five hundred this latter condition very likely accident never mentioned again then was pay twelve thousand talents dollars yearly instalments one thousand each and give twenty hostages among whom was his own son was place the disposition the romans the whole the country this side the taurus which belonged him that say asia minor with the exception the two cilicias north the taurus the halys was the boundary thus antiochus was yield all that possessed phrygia was afterwards moot point whether pamphylia was also included therein livy and the fragments polybius throw light upon and the whole the geography these countries very obscure far however can understand appian pamphylia not remain under the rule antiochus nor was bestowed upon eumenes but existed independent state between both moreover the king was not meddle with the affairs europe without leave from rome nor wage war with nations which were allies the romans unless were attacked was give his ships war even the
triremes all but ten keep elephants enlist mercenaries from countries which were subject the romans pay specified sum eumenes and also deliver hannibal and some others whom had received his court these last were added only for the sake appearances give good colouring the demand for the surrender hannibal but these made their escape this happened the year the definitive peace being concluded somewhat later rashly undertaken war could have led one battle such peace but that prince capable making should have been called the great quite inconceivable and yet had still immense empire large germany france and spain put together the following year manlius the successor scipio took the command quite impatient something this and the hope booty led him compliance with the wishes the asiatics undertake campaign against the galatians gallogrecians phrygia about the time pyrrhus the gauls overran macedonia and had forced their way far delphi thenwhether moved the greeks relate awful natural phenomena allured the accounts which they had heard the beautiful countries asiathey marched off out greece eastward thrace there many them remained and established their rule others twenty thousand number crossed two divisions the one over the hellespont the other over the bosporus being
favoured the feuds the asiatic princes here they gained settlements ancyran phrygia the northern coast just later times the normans neustria and henceforth they lived thirty free towns land which meant nature the seat the greatest wealth and happiness but which now under the rule barbarians has become wilderness there were three tribes them the trocmi tolistoboii and tectosages the two first which seem have been formed the course their migrations for not meet with them elsewhere certainly with the third they united themselves with the bithynians among whom two small kingdoms arose the latter were thracians and they dwelt between nicomedia and heraclea during the persian domination they were under their native princes but after the breaking the persian and the macedonian empires which had always been least consolidated asia minor they widened their sway and became proportionally important nicomedes who was then king took the gauls among whom there were still but ten thousand armed men into his pay defeated his rival and founded the bithynian state which now became hellenized from that time the gauls sold their aid whosoever wanted and made the whole western asia tributary themselves this part history still very confused but may disentangled
have many materials for they were defeated antiochus soter which they withdrew into the mountains and when circumstances had changed they burst forth again every one paid them tribute escape their ravages when the war broke out between ptolemy euergetes and seleucus callinicus and afterwards between the former and antiochus hierax they sold themselves being thoroughly faithless now one now the other and they became the scourge the whole asia until the astonishment everybody attalus pergamus refusing pay them tribute any longer attacked and defeated them which only accounted for the fact that sloth had made them utterly effeminate and unwarlike just like the goths whom belisarius encountered italy from this blow they never quite recovered yet they still retained considerable influence asia was always divided and although antiochus was living their neighbourhood was too busy notwithstanding able protect that part phrygia which bordered the country where they dwelt they therefore went raising tribute far and wide and now after the downfall antiochus the asiatic peoples were afraid that they should not able defend themselves this gave manlius opportunity taking the field the defender these against the galatians those barbarians had answered his summons yield with stolida ferocia marched through
phrygia and attacked them their mountains without however exterminating them they remained there and retained the celtic language for remarkably long period even down the times augustus degrees they also hellenized themselves and such find them have been the days paul the war was most desirable for the inhabitants asia minor but thoroughly unjust the side the romans manlius undertook contrary the expressed will the decem legati who followed him was ended two campaigns and brought the romans other fruits but the booty and the sum money which may perhaps have been paid for the countries between western asia and the land the galatians were not the subjects but the allies rome the gauls suffered such severe defeats that thenceforth they lived quietly and subjection the romans the romans now divided their conquests eumenes who until then had had quite small dominion very much like that petty german prince now became great king mysia lydia phrygia the hellespont and great phrygia the two were afterwards made one under the name the kingdom asia and the inhabitants were called asians ionia with the exception smyrna phoca erythr and some other greek towns which retained their freedom became his was great and
enviable empire but for all that feeble one owing asiatic effeminacy the rhodians got caria and lycia with the exception telmissus which heaven knows why fell the share eumenes this was for little republic immense windfall these were fine rich countries from which they might draw millions our money the taxes among the ancients were very heavy and mostly land being third the whole produce revenues like these made the rhodians very rich and they spent them partly armaments and partly the embellishment their city which even without this was already beautiful the rhodians are thoroughly respectable people the romans themselves acknowledged that they had none the levitas grcorum about them but were quite their equals severitas disciplin impeachment scipio end scipio africanus and hannibal domestic affairs porcius cato the contradictions which according livy were everywhere rife with regard scipios end are remarkable instance the way which even impossible statements were got and see from thence that even time which contemporary history was already written when the work fabius was ended and that acilius began these accounts were very little substantiated not know for certain the year which scipio died what quoted livy from the speech tib gracchus must deemed
worth more than the stories the annalists there doubt that scipio was once called upon the senate the petillii answer the charge having received sums money from antiochus and not having accounted the republic for those which had been gained during the course the war this kind impeachment one the earliest which meet with among the romans the consuls might indeed freely dispose the manubia they might distribute them among the soldiers deposit them the rarium but they were always ready give account the romans money matters were very particular with regard this point scipio sent for his books and produced them the senate but his brother snatched them out his hands and destroyed them saying that was shame when and his brother had made the state rich ask account for such trifle million drachm thus dollars were already then trifle hereupon impeachment was brought against scipio spoke few proud words and then waswhich can hardly otherwise than authenticthat cried out this the day that conquered hannibal zama which are always wont offer sacrifice let those who are well disposed follow the tribunes alone are said have staid behind this accusation may perhaps made agree with the fact that gracchus
himself had wanted have scipio arrested and that this when the prtor terentius culleo was about try the case scipio had all haste come from etruria and rescued his brother from the beadles and therefore africanus plus quam civiles animos gerebat too was impeached either not wait for this prosecution and retired liternum latin colony colonia maritima between cum and minturn had lived there already before thus much certain that the last years his life not pass rome that lived liternum exile and not for his own pleasure becomes probable from the circumstance that before his death some one else was princeps senatus such exile was easy bring about for settled liternum citizen had thereby renounced the right roman citizenship scipio with his qustor and legate was found guilty having embezzled the sum with which had been charged was not addicted but his property was seized the state and said not have been sufficient cover the demand conclude from thence that was innocent would quite absurd for might have been spendthrift the meanwhile after the first punic war the number the tribes had been raised five and thirty great part the sabines had acquired the full right citizenship and had
formed two new tribes the quirina and velina this was nearly sixty years after the last increase and thus there were considerable signs already state political stagnation the same time perhaps early before the first punic war many towns were made prfectures with crite rights during the second punic war there were four prtors and while yet lasted their number was increased six like sicily spain now became province rather was divided into two provinces citerior and ulterior which two prtors were sent southern italy had likewise taken the form province owing the war with hannibal and continued such for some time after the prtor there was most likely tarentum bruttium but gaul was not yet reduced provinci formam and there was course prtor there the greatest change which reached deepest and had the most lasting consequences had been caused the falling away many peoples hannibal they were punished and the places which had belonged them lost all the privileges italian allies some were treated conquered their lands being either confiscated merely left them sufferance others who had submitted had but met with forbearance this was the fate great many places samnium and apulia which were severed from their communities
those which had remained faithful kept indeed their ancient constitution the lucanians the war with hannibal had their own prtor whom they elected themselves they may have still enjoyed this privilege but all their subject towns which had revolted were detached from them the bruttians who had persisted the longest their revolt were altogether deprived their constitution they were mere dediticii more allies all they had some them become serfs and the whole their land was confiscated uncertain whether they had been formerly the same footing with the samnites and lucanians being greek descent they were most likely treated foreigners yet they had still held honourable position which was now gone tarentum lost all its rights and lingered forsaken within its own walls until little little fell nothing this change among the allies made more difficult for those who remained fulfil their engagements rome than before and owing the rebellion likewise bitter and longlived hatred had grown between rome and many the italian peoples and what had much exhausted the allies was the drain upon their citizens many whom had taken advantage the isopolity settle rome the colonies some the latin colonies moreover had neglected their duty twelve out thirty
having furnished contingent during the expedition hasdrubal and now when circumstances allowed their rights were abridged the traces the war with hannibal had never been done away the samnites apulians and lucanians had already been hardly dealt with before etruria alone found herself state high prosperity many colonies were planted the south italy not much for securitys sake thus provide for the poorer romans the veterans scipios army were rewarded special grant land apulia and lucania which the first example known provision made for veterans large scale had the second decade livy might perhaps discover some earlier instances but indeed they can only have been single cases the condition italy must have been one extreme distress the price every thing was unnaturally high and owing the heavy wartaxes the middle classes must have been utterly impoverished the latter periods the war meet with public debt which was repaid three instalments but the macedonian war had drained the exchequer that the third instalment was made public lands the roman people itself was affected its very lifes blood the war had cost immense host men and notwithstanding the census now gives like number have only proof that the meanwhile crowd foreigners especially
freedmen had been received citizens and that thus the body the roman commonalty had become quite different thing from what had been before those who had stood the war were for the most part grown wretchedly poor all this misery not detected livys narrative but know from other sources that rome almost continual famine and epidemics were raging many families had their estates the falernian country and campania which districts were entirely laid waste others which had possessed landed property the revolted provinces had lost their all that this struggle quite destroyed the wealth the nation the greek towns croton and others were never able recover another consequence was that the soldiers remained for years under arms that the legions which had been composed men enlisted for campaign were converted into standing army this continued the case after the war and the soldiers became accustomed look upon themselves permanent order which they had never been before the legions were disbanded every year and newly raised the next this condition the preservation republican freedom was now changed the war with hannibal and thus were the seeds here sown the later troubles owing the great confiscations immense landed estates had been gained
the possession which was divided between the great men among the patricians and plebeians there was one now control them and the licinian law had become dead letter that time not soul actually thought danger yet the beginning dissolution most decidedly existed already said that owing the victories asia luxury and its concomitant vices had spread but this was accidental symptom the real cause lay deeper after such long savage and destructive wars which many deeds outrage and ferocity had been wrought which the poor had become poorer and poorer and the middle classes had gone down more and more whilst the rich were crammed with wealth many things must have changed for the worse the same soldiers who formerly had earned glory under scipio and then hungry plunderers went asia enriched themselves immensely and returned with gotten treasures they had real wants and not know how use their suddenly acquired riches even the character the great men every thing else everywhere meet with great alteration the dismal spectacle utter degeneracy already preparing itself the generals appear like robbers they carry wars merely for the sake pillage and booty and the exceptions among them are few and far between the
men high rank are overbearing towards the allies former times roman magistrate when travelling through italy would put the house his own guestfriend but was now customary for such travellers everywhere received with pomp the games were got style and scale which required immense fortune there were one funeral less than hundred and fifty gladiators the forum banquets were given the people was already the fashion seek for choice specimens art and luxury the officers and the nobles filled their houses with furniture tapestry and plate every description brutal expenditure wealth got vogue judicious and liberal use riches being one the most difficult things the world thus when several years ago the inhabitants dittmarsch all once made great deal money immediately gave rise sluttish wastefulness until before long they were reduced again the cooks who hitherto had been the most despised slaves rome now became the most highly valued earlier times the consul lived like the peasant only the pontiffs whose bills fare may still read macrobius were held keep good table the most dignified canons with the athenians was quite different the greek naturally very temperate and the italian can too but when the latter has opportunity feasting makes
beast himself moreover although the constitution was most democratical appearance yet already see the overweening pride the nobles the increase the rich were almost above punishment quinctius flamininus the brother titus amuse his catamite caused man who was either convict gallic hostage beheaded for which cato expelled him from the senate and though fifty years afterwards polybius conscientiously places the romans above the greeks peculation and extortions from the allies were notwithstanding very common may see from excellent fragment cato sumtu suo the gem the collection fronto shows that towards the end the sixth century was the general belief that the servants the state seized upon every opportunity feathering their own nests all distinctions between the different orders had entirely ceased the only thing looked was whether man were noble not the patricians order having quite lost their importance the last their privileges that one consul should always belong one the two orders was done away with the time the war with perseus the patrician houses were nearly extinct for the diles only this was still the rule but the case the prtorship was altogether abolished was however extremely difficult for plebeian rise who was not high rank for only
few novi homines like cato could make their way and the whole the nobility seem have been league check such intrusion the other hand the city was very much embellished stately buildings were erected and instead the courts justice being held any longer with other covering but heaven was done our german forefathers basilic were built this name was derived from the under which the athens used sit was triple portico which the judges assembled the open air though not under the open sky cato was the first who built basilica porcia the forum and several others followed they were afterwards enclosed with walls and when the christian religion was introduced into rome this form was deemed the one best suited the christian worship the different sto might assigned separate places the men and the matrons being the aisles each side and the clergy the middle the tribunal was the high altar and the throne the bishop hence the name basilica was applied all christian churches even when they were longer this form the material the buildings was still the old simple one the style the ancient doric tuscan marble was not yet seen porcius cato the most remarkable man
that age quite man the old times the surname priscus however merely indicates his latin origin from tusculum the account him plutarch excellent his life may understood without any knowledge the constitution deep insight into politics nothing else was needed but keen perception individual character which was plutarchs strong point perhaps rome never again gave birth original genius his whilst all around him had their science and erudition from greece cato had from himself learned greek only late life his language his style his knowledge were altogether roman more versatile mind than his the world has never known was great statesmanhis censorship was distinguished onean excellent agriculturist active man every business life gifted with remarkable eloquence which was pure nature and not all formed after artificial rules and was also very eminent scholar indefatigable research excellent prosewriter his own way although harsh and uncouth livy who otherwise fond him applies him jest the phrase qui vivo allatrare ejus scipionis magnitudinem solitus erat his peculiarities were those man low birth who being endowed with immense energy had worked his way dint through countless difficulties all his life long kept feud with the nobles and the rich abhorred their manners from the
bottom his heartthere was affectation the only one like him feeling was his colleague the censorship and the tribunate valerius flaccus cato was fanatical roman bore hatred against every thing that was polished and elegant his nationality therefore led him dwell fondly the past looked upon the men his day quite degenerate his ideal dated hundred years back and with him the height happiness was simplicity thriftiness and stern morality his constitution was iron strength his eightysixth year still carried troublesome lawsuit and even late his ninetieth impeached servius sulpicius galba stood without flinching for romes supremacy but the same time had extraordinary sense justice though not like the greeks yet defended the rhodians likewise the lusitanians against the perjury and the extortions galba the whole very like the great german characters the sixteenth century whom what called coarseness means deserves that name whilst cato was almost the only really great man virtue was then the wane and genius becoming more and more rare the moneyed interest also those days was already great importance since the acquisition sicily there had been wide field opened for employment capital people went into the provinces make their fortunes rome canon law was forbidden

father the two fated brothers became consul and went spain was who had deeply deplored that scipio tried set himself above the law but who not wish him punished like any other citizen and scipio had afterwards chosen him for his soninlaw that time the feeling hostility had already been more widely kindled the celtiberians who had spread from the sources the ebro the threefold border the mancha andalusia and valencia and chiefly dwelt new castile and western aragon the provinces soria and cuena had never been subject the carthaginians but had furnished them with mercenaries they also the romans they now got involved war with the romans who endeavoured reduce them they were the bravest people spain with them gracchus concluded peace the conditions which are unknown but they were fair that these tribes who reality had wish whatever for war ever afterwards looked upon the greatest good which could befall them they were only allowed have them the whole family the gracchi distinguished for extraordinary mildness and kindness which otherwise are quite foreign the roman character had his successors kept the peace the celtiberians would have become true and useful allies the romans the marsians and pelignians other
generals however extended the roman rule the west spain the vaccans north the tagus and the lusitanians must have been brought under subjection between and yet this was not for long owing the extortions the generals the meantime new thunderstorm gathered the east philips reign had lasted long while but made excellent use his time strengthen his kingdom his expectations from the war against antiochus had not been fulfilled but had considerably enlarged his dominions was again possession demetrias and part magnesia that hemmed thessaly the dolopians had remained under his sway although they were detached from his country also had athamania and had gotten again the greek towns the thracian coast nos maronea abdera and others which had formerly been egyptian the romans had let him quietly for while but now they began craftily undermine his rule they gave their encouragement when amynander drove the macedonian garrisons from athamania they received embassies which they themselves had set foot from thessaly and the towns the thracian coast bearing complaints philips encroachments they must have held the conviction that had other object but thus strengthen himself until should able regain his former might but philip all his preparations was too cautious

their arms against the inhabitants one hundred and fifty thousand epirotes are said have been either slain led away slaves and seventy places have been destroyed this horrible shows the rank degeneracy the roman people there longer any balance its different elements but only the dead weight one promiscuous mass slavery strips man half his virtue but absolute liberty what one lists creates double vice rulers the world the romans thought themselves privileged any thing and everything after such deed this cannot agree with plutarch ranking milius among great and virtuous men throughout the whole greece and particularly botia things were just bad the sword was put into the hands the partisans the romans and their rage was ruthless tolia all greek countries there were two factions the one devoted and the other hostile the romans the roman party ruled without any one control and the lengths which went its outrages beggar all belief besides other atrocities broke into the senate house and butchered all the senators who were accused being friendly the macedonians roman troops were sent thither under the command bbius this frightful state things extended likewise the achans there the party perseus had not been very strong

and the parties regularly tried those who were brought guilty should then punished without mercy but the envoys would have nothing say this they wanted give the list after the executions only and when they were urged mention names they said that all those who had been strategi were guilty then xeno who had formerly been strategus got and declared that was conscious his innocence that would take his trial before tribunal achaia and this were not sufficient would even defend himself rome the roman commissioners eagerly caught this and they had list drawn callicrates those who were sent italy and judged there there were more than thousand these some them made their escape for which they were denounced convicted offenders and the punishment death was inflicted upon them when they were taken the rest were not brought before court justice all but were distributed hostages the municipal towns was only after the lapse seventeen years that the three hundred who were still alive were let this occasion polybius also came rome his lot was soon bettered for got intimate with several families high rank and milius paullus himself made him the companion his sons that might guide them into
greek learning macedon was nominally declared free but half the taxes were laid upon which had been formerly paid the kingsan example how the romans still exacted tribute from those countries which they not convert into roman provinces the country was divided into four states this splitting into cantons the strangest shape the taking away all connubium and commercium between them and the geographical division these districts which tribes belonging the same stock were torn asunder and others which were quite distinct were united are masterpieces macchiavellian policy those which suited each other were disjoined and those which clashed were jumbled together order that moral strength and unity might ever grow the whole the consequence this was that the power the macedonians was completely broken and yet the romans were behaving all the time they were giving them republican constitution every one these quarters they granted synedrium and pretext removing those who were dangerous this new equality they drove all the men rank and distinction out the country the advantage this arrangement showed itself afterwards the rebellion the pseudophilip the triumph milius paullus the most brilliant any which had been seen until then owing the quantity costly things displayed the

and while the debates the subject were going old cato incessantly urged the senate that carthage should destroyed the government the world had given the senate importance which made for the loss power home from the growth the democratic principle and the senators felt more and more like kings now the senate with regard carthage was divided between two opinionsthe one blind dogged hatred that carthage should destroyed the bottom which was the consciousness that rome was the object universal hatred the other that cornelius scipio nasica which held the other hand that carthage was godsend nothing else could keep rome well balanced nasica seems have been fully aware the actual condition the state and were many others but with regard the remedy opinions were divided some thought that there was help for and that therefore one ought ahead and make the most short life cato was one these others like nasica believed that the evil might least checked superficial means thorough reform could not perhaps carried out small party which afterwards came forward with tib gracchus its head tried root out the disease desperate remedies whether this justice carthage nasica sprang indeed from love righteousness more than can tell

against rome only and was therefore required them that they should surrender all their ships war and all the catapults and that moreover they should deliver all their arms and stores rome was also declared would fully protect them and the peace with masinissa would sanctioned hard they felt this the carthaginians yielded and the whole the arms were brought thousand waggons and under the eyes the roman commissioners the roman camp the romans first landing had demanded supply corn for their army and received the grain from the magazines the city which was thus very nearly reduced state famine with this the carthaginians thought have done enough but now the ambassadors received the last audience they were led through the ranks the whole army the tribunal the consuls who now told them that all that had been done betokened the good will the carthaginian government yet that the latter was not even master the town that long this strong city was standing rome was not safe and that carthage therefore must demolished and its inhabitants were build for themselves open town the inland country two german miles away from the sea when the ambassadors remonstrated the consuls said that
they had promised safety the men and not the walls that the people should not harmed and they might just well live ten roman miles from the sea those who dwelt rome the outbursts rage and despair this infamous deceit were avail the last awful prayer was that the consuls would before the ambassadors returned cause the roman fleet make its appearance before carthage strike with dismay this was treason them was prompted despair those among them who had advised their countrymen yield saw full well that they went home they should fall victims the rage the people and they therefore remained under the protection the romans those who came back refused answer the people who had gone out meet them and they weeping brought the answer into the senate was resolved die upon the ruins the city the gates were immediately shut and all the romans and italians the town were seized and tortured death this the consuls had not expected they were indeed well informed menmanilius was even highly distinguished juristbut they were unfit for war may that the fate the town appeared themselves dreadful that their heart sickened and they went work without spirit had they once

himself uncertain according some dishonourable means yet was man talent his very opposite was tib sempronius gracchus who was plebeian house but most ancient nobility the latter was the head the popular party pompeius led his army against the numantines and was unsuccessful they took his camp and brought him very great straits being this plight offered peace the numantines but only for forms sake were give hostages whom was return them they were also pay certain sum and promise serve the field this they also but this most reasonable peace not please rome nor was pompeius fool enough believe that would his successor order the senate disregarded altogether the numantines sent ambassadors rome and appealed the treaties which they were borne out the roman staffofficers but the senate annulled the peace pompeius himself doing his utmost bring this about that might not called account for the way which had conducted the war hostilities were renewed greater scale and few years afterwards the command fell hostilius mancinus man who had the luck gain great celebrity and sort moral notoriety which indeed very doubtful nature the frightened spaniards had abandoned numantia its fate and mancinus had reached far the suburbana the
gardens and cemeteries the town there was driven back engagement the numantines pursued and the romans retreating blind haste got into place from which there was way out that they had make their minds either sue for peace perish first the numantines would have nothing say the conditions offered mancinus favourable they were was only tib gracchus then serving qustor who could save the army the numantines had not forgotten the equitable peace which his father had made but the remembrance his upright conduct towards all the celtiberians was dear them that they accepted the son mediator being convinced that meant honestly great was the respect which was held them that betook himself the midst them numantia get back his accountbooks which well the camp had fallen into their hands and these were also returned him uninjured the army which without reckoning the allies numbered twenty thousand men was allowed march off without disgrace and independence and friendship were stipulated for numantia mancinus afterwards played rome the same part which postumius had done after the caudine peace recommended the senate yield himself and the officers atone for the unauthorized peace the people agreed this far was concerned but threw out
the clause the officers out regard for tib gracchus mancinus was delivered the nobleminded numantines would not have him that the curse broken oath might fall upon those who were guilty the war lasted yet few years longer without any result that the romans were driven spite the laws appian says elect scipio africanus consul ten years had already passed away since his first consulship and the leges annales could not have prescribed age which had not reached already perhaps there was law that one should consul twice scipio went forth with many recruits allies and volunteers from all parts with numidians and men from the far east against that small people root out from the earth all the proffers the numantines were rejected scipio found great degeneracy the roman troops and cost him vast deal trouble restore discipline the loose morals and the luxury which were rife among individuals were likewise spreading the army purified and then marched with sixty thousand men against numantia this city was surrounded three sides the douro and lay therefore isthmus which was strongly fortified around the town the circumference not being more than three roman miles one german scipio now drew line pallisades
with rampart and behind second onejust plat was shut the spartansand here distributed his army these lines placed engines for hurling missiles with which the romans tried keep off their desperate foes they wanted destroy them hunger for while some them escaped the douro which the besieged also got supplies but cut them off even from this sinking above the town huge beams armed with saws into the river that the rafts with flour could longer float down that way how long this dreadful blockade lasted more than can tell once however some numantines climbed over the walls and came distant town where some hundred youths enthusiastically took arms and thus general rising against the romans was the eve bursting forth when scipio found this out forthwith marched thither and had the hands those who were guilty cut off such atrocity stamps the man the numantines when they had fed first the dead bodies the enemy and then those their own countrymen and gone through all those horrors which missolunghi had suffer wished length capitulate scipio demanded that their arms should given and that they should surrender discretion they asked for three days which they spent freeing their wives and
children death from slavery that few them only came out who were like skeletons these scipio picked out fifty for his triumph who seem have been beheaded afterwards the rest were sold but they are said have broken out with such rage some them killing themselves and others murdering their masters that after short time not numantine was left alive the place where the town had stood from henceforth became waste the servile war sicily acquisition the kingdom pergamus aristonicus domestic affairs the punishment for foul deed was not slow overtaking the romans even before the fall numantia servile war broke out sicily though indeed this does not much belong roman grecian history was brought the depopulation the island owing the many wars which famine and pestilence were raging germany during the thirty years war twentyfour years had not yet passed since the first punic war when the second completed the misery sicily was state desolation like that ireland after the peace limerick the times william much the land was made ager publicus and thus fell into the hands speculators this way there arose large estates sicily which were chiefly used for grazing thus according the codex theodosianus nearly the
whole lucania bruttium and calabria the days honorius and arcadius was pasture land which the owners who were partly romans partly siciliotes kept large studs horses and herds cattle herdsmen italy are degenerate race men they are almost all them far know the states the church and the kingdom naplesin tuscany there are few them the associates robbers the herdsman bad and robberlike the peasant the other hand respectable these large estates there was immense number slavesoften many thousands together one alone the traffic slaves owing the wars and the continual piracy those times had reached fearful height that the slavemarket delos ten thousand are said have been sold one day and they were had for mere trifle they were treated with the greatest cruelty and had work the fields chains course there were among them many respectable men from all parts carthaginians achans macedonians celtiberians and others who deserved quite different fate and could not but thirst for the blood their tyrants thus the servile war broke out sicily and not wondered that there was then another these risings greece the cause was everywhere the same greece tillage had formerly been mostly the business the freedmen and was only
late that had fallen into the hands the slaves the war had now reached its fourth year several roman armies had been utterly routed and required consular one under rupilius reduce the island for the slaves were masters the strongest places enna and tauromenium and they had for their leader eunus syrian who like jean franois domingo the year put the diadem due form the struggle was carried with the same relentless cruelty which slaves have met with everywhere the west indies and north america sicily was laid utterly waste and thirty years afterwards the same circumstances led the same results the details are awfully interesting yet have said before they are not their place here the meanwhile attalus philometor pergamus the son eumenes died and with him the race philetrus became extinct the first kings pergamus whom the romans had raised greatness were the whole clever men and princes and under their rule the country flourished this state things was desirable one although looked upon moral point view much might said against but the last attalus was tyrant and wicked wretch such only met with the east where certain perversity reaches its highest pitch and takes delight what most
unnatural and revolting word was incarnate fiend like sultan ibrahim the only art which employed himself was that cultivating deadly plants and preparing poison was sport him get those who were his nearest kindred out the world bequeathed the whole his kingdom the romans and indeed could not well have done otherwise every one his dispositions had still approved the romans who would hardly have acknowledged the rule any one else they took property which right belonged them very much master might take the goods one his freedmen who had not been fully emancipated and had died without leaving will thus rome had new province which however was won the sword aristonicus bastard son eumenes laid claim the throne according the notions the east this defect birth was not bar the succession that but for the will attalus would have been the lawful heir had very little trouble getting hold the diadem soon after the death his brother for the people had horror the roman rule and they had learned know the tyranny and rapacity the roman prtors and proconsuls who made their appearance every year many towns declared for him others like ephesus which had lately gained their freedom

only after the laws gracchus during the earlier times trial was required any case delictum manifestum the identity the person being proved the prtor immediately enforced the law and that was all other cases criminal causes and those suits which were not brought before the centum viri the decision one arbiter was needed before the prtor could pass sentence which might acted upon the complaint was laid before the prtor who after thirty days named judge the latter gave judgment according certain fixed rules from which there was further appeal for the appeal which there had once been the people had been done away with whilst for anything that was not judicium publicum none perhaps had ever been allowed since the seventh century several pleas for which formerly special qusitores had been appointed from whom they came before the popular tribunals were now judged according the common course law especially the actiones repetundarum the complaints the unfortunate provincials against their governors for these however several judges were granted but this single judge the case might these several judges were always senators and this was indeed strong tie which the senate strengthened its authority but these courts were detestable the most
scandalous judgments were given and the senator who lot had become judex allowed himself bribed the most barefaced manner one making any secret nor indeed was any body ashamed doing thus those who were not bought formed but small exception and that perhaps merely from calculation the right bringing action made the provinces yet worse off than they had been utterly debarred from for the governor had plunder much the more that might able bribe his judges this reminds the saying the neapolitan minister the prince canosa eccentric but witty man said that where out the kingdom naples could one get many false witnesses for carlino about fourpence each and that one wanted quantity them they were had cheaper still thus the senators rome merely asked how many thousands will you give that may acquit you one crow does not pick out the eyes the other this was revolting and was clear that would bring the state ruin change was necessary and that gracchus was certainly the best things were though the other hand might also have consequences cast his eyes upon that body men which now some measure filled the place middle class although sometimes possessing immense riches was

and take for instance onefifth instead the tenth which was their due return for this the knights would guarantee them impunity should they prosecuted for extortion this was monstrous abuse occasioned accidental circumstances but for rome and italy the change was improvement and was the whole for all those places which the farming companies not extend this fell upon the senators like thunderbolt and when independent body judges had now been formed gracchus went still farther substituted their jurisdiction for those popular tribunals which were not worth anything and which henceforth are only met with exception this was setting bounds democracy where democracy was longer its right place order put better blood into the veins the thirtyfive tribes wished extend the full right citizenship the latins among whom there were some forty colonial towns besides the old latin cities they had existed for three hundred years and had for two centuries been entirely amalgamated language and manners with the romans and all likelihood meant form them into new tribes the italian allies the other hand from lucania the march ancona nay all the italian districts far the alps wished raise that position which the latins then held that say give

and slain gracchus leaped from the temple diana down the sharp steep the aventine and sprained his ankle not being able find horse leaning his friends could hardly reach the pons sublicius the two friends pomponius and ltorius who were knights and formed honourable exception the majority the higher classes fought like horatius cocles the bridge keep the pursuers bay and allowed themselves cut down the meanwhile gracchus fled across the tiber into sacred grove lucus furiarum which however not shelter him opimius had promised for his head its weight gold according the most likely account faithful slave him the friendly service killing him anagnian septimuleius got the head and filled with molten lead upwards three thousand men were denounced partisans gracchus and nearly all them were put death opimius few only may have made their escape this war extermination was waged against all who were any way distinguished was downright butchery like that the year naples for two years the bloodshed lasted and these murderers called themselves boni homines boni cives there were many renegades and there doubt but that carbo was very early one them became consul and then defended opimius against the charges brought against him the

for soon marius stood for the consulship was blinded his rage that became his enemy this very day one meets among the high english nobility with men like metellus who look upon the privileges their order the first inviolable rights and whenever offences committed any their own body come light will step with their protection prevent exposure thus the remarkable character metellus becomes quite clear was estimable for the integrity his motives but utterly incapable being just spurned all the offers jugurtha against whom used his own punic arts that that prince was obliged disarm entirely the price hopes which were never fulfilled and when jugurtha wished actually buy himself off from the ruin which clearly saw before his eyes metellus put forth conditions which would have rendered him quite defenceless last metellus demanded that should appear person this jugurtha refused and the war broke out afresh metellus carried for two years and though was sometimes worsted deserves very great praise for the manner which overcame the difficulties which had encounter several his undertakings are some the most brilliant history jugurtha the whole avoided pitched battles risked engagement only once and then was beaten now again see that mixture cowardice
