conflict brilliant victory was gained most the ambrones being destroyed notwithstanding which the romans who were without entrenchments now passed anxious night which they were busily throwing works the next battle was not fought the following day had been expected but the day after most likely because the teutones and the rest the ambrones had only just now arrived marius laid all his plans with the talent true general and sent claudius marcellusa man whose family was always distinguished being undoubtedly grandson that worthy marcellus well known the iberian war who had five times been consulwith division allies would seem attack the enemys rear yet even before this the fury the teutones had spent itself vain against the steadfastness and dogged resolution the romans and the more was summer for the men the south owing their more muscular frame are able stand both heat and frost better than others the italians napoleons russian campaign suffered much less than the northern nations and therefore one might easily believe the natives rome bore the glowing heat the sun much better than the teutones the romans who were posted hill awaited the onset the barbarians these were beaten back and when they were
endeavouring rally the plain marcellus fell upon them from behind part them tried make their escape and were overpowered and slain the gallic tribes the prince the teutones was taken prisoner the sequani and the remnant his army retreated within their rampart waggons but the romans now broke and nearly the whole the nation was destroyed some very few only being made slaves half the danger was now warded off soon afterwards the cimbri burst upon italy through tyrol and the alps trent and this was not from any fault catulus but was altogether owing their overwhelming numbers and the terror which they spread far and wide the account florus the manner which the cimbri opened the way for themselves quite childish just these had been the dullest savages and had wanted stop the tide the adige with their hands this shows what homo umbraticus that writer was there are indeed some fords the adige and passing such river one makes the cavalry cross higher and somewhat lower down close column infantry which will break the force moderate stream this the cimbri may also have tried thinking perhaps that with their huge bodies they would able stem the flood but
the adige near legnano such thing impossible afterwards they are said have thrown trees into the river dam which also incredible they wished rather have bridge and destroy that the romans means their floats timbers and this they succeeded doing the romans being posted each end the bridge both sides the stream one their two divisions was cut off from the other and was obliged surrender the cimbri but these with unwonted humanity let free this however true that crossing the most impassable parts the alps they glided their large shields sleighs down the steepest declivities this irruption catulus fell back far the yet beyond the whole country north that river was laid waste the towns mantua verona brescia which were left the protection their walls defended themselves but the open places were destroyed from the winter the following summer the cimbri most unaccountably remained that side the marius heard gaul the irruption the barbarians and ordered his army march genua liguria would seem and went himself rome here every one was now full admiration for him and the feeling that was the only man who could save the country was become general that even the oligarchs were for his
being made consul for the fifth time people were eager gain his goodwill that they offered him triumph but this declined until should have destroyed the cimbri and his assurance communicated itself every one accordingly united his army with that catulus who had remained command proconsul they both them now passed the with somewhat more than fiftytwo thousand men said that the cimbri knew nothing the defeat the teutones which downright absurdity impossible that from autumn the end july they should not have got any news was surely for this very reason that they asked marius for land and places abode they felt that half their power had been overthrown they also demanded this for their brethren these must have been the tigurini whether the cimbri now wished secure the passes gaul that they might keep the road over the little bernard open for any emergency and this was why they came vercell uncertain yet notwithstanding all the variations the readings there seems doubt that battle was fought near vercelli the declivity the alps for one cannot see how any body should have thought placing this corner lombardy writers call the spot campi raudii the battle contrary the roman custom
was announced three days beforehand and the third day before the calends the sextilis july the calendar was then was fought much time had the cimbri spent their ravages since the beginning winter this unwholesome aguish country where the water bad epidemics also had already broken out among them the day the battle marius put the army catulus the centre disposing his own the two wings the account which found plutarch only confused that nothing distinct can made out incredible that the cimbri should have formed great square each side which was threequarters german mile long the men the outside ranks having are told their girdles linked together with chains such mass would amount many millions men marius said have placed his troops that the sun and the wind were the faces the barbarians such thing may history may fiction catulus had stand the brunt the battle least the fight was hottest where was and yet was only proof party spirit when people disputed whether was marius catulus that the victory was due for seems beyond all doubt that marius decided the battle the wings and thus had the chief merit the cimbrians fled within their rampart waggons where even
the women and children fought and killed themselves last great many were taken prisoners the alps blocked their retreat short every thing belonging the cimbri which had crossed these mountains was cut off all but the tribe the aduatici who had settled hereabouts the lower rhine where they must therefore have had fixed abodes one time reward for his unexampled achievements marius had now his sixth consulship given him led the most brilliant triumph which any general had ever had but even then already showed how much his head was turned entered the senate his triumphal garments there was belief that some one before him had been six times consul but this can longer ascertained the ancients themselves could not tell perhaps valerius corvus was six times consul may however have been that what accounted his sixth consulship one his family was mistaken for him marius was called the third founder rome after romulus and camillus but this consulship although marius last became useful the state had such dismal consequences make one wish that had died the day his triumph then his memory would have been glorious and blessed and would have thrown even scipio into the shade marius sixth
consulship apuleius saturninus servilius glaucia marius was not the man who could play his part well quiet peaceful times and yet rome was hastening towards dissolution way which compelled him act there are very many kinds courage the greatest men have owned there courage with regard danger which either looks death the face with indifference forgets altogether the excitement action this fine quality itself but does not follow that the motive for its display should noble alone whom this constancy allied pure mind and who conscious lofty aim will enjoy with the full sense personal freedom and enabled achieve great things many are wanting this sort prowess who yet possess determined moral courage owing which they hold themselves above the opinion those around them being all the same them whether they misjudged not others who the hour danger show the courage lions are exceedingly timid this respect and afraid acting conviction which has been branded the worlds anathema was this latter sense that marius was weak for one was say that let himself used tool the men who exercised such influence during his sixth consulship this would making him out have been most pitiful wretch whereas the clue his conduct
that was one time afraid the demagogues and another the senate deplorable although partial weakness great man who had greatness character marius had joined himself with sad knave get his sixth consulship this was apuleius saturninus who undeservedly enough often named with the gracchi although there cannot wider interval than that between them and saturninus was man like catiline one indeed whom the like seldom seen for though one can understand how ambition will lead people blindfold into acts dangerous daring yet how man could have taken his head mad all but incomprehensible would seem that his was revolutionary mind that formed clear notion what things would come being utterly regardless institutions and government and only thinking violence and confusion had sprung from one the richest and most eminent plebeian families just the french revolution men the first nobility put themselves the head the rabble not recollect whether him servilius glaucia that cicero says that one had been gifted with more malignant wit was this means that they managed the people had started life aristocrat there were that time eight qustorships which were given partly consulars and partly other persons they were places with income attached them one them being
the qustura ostiensis which had the charge the granaries rome saturninus had qustor availed himself the privilege peculatus taken the men rank but when the tables were suddenly turned and the oligarchs were longer able screen the sins their own body owing honest party having been formed from both factions under the lead the straightforward memmius got liable the punishment being deposed and threw himself into the arms the mob was conspiracy the dregs the upper and middle classes now became tribune the people and behaved the most savage manner towards the very first men for instance the censors and others when his standing the second time for the tribuneship another candidate nonius was set against him hounded the rabble against that unfortunate man that they murdered him and thus made himself force tribune again the magistrates had more any authority those who had the power just what they liked his accomplice was servilius glaucia like him man very high rank not freedman might inferred from his name similar manner scipio was nicknamed serapio from actor whom bore likeness what these two really wanted hard say their madness went even utter recklessness might assumed that they aimed tyranny for one
them but they believed that marius would allow such thing this were just great insanity that the drunkard shakspeares tempest must deem many the men that time have been downright madmen robespierre also can never said what purpose hadvery likely had none whatever thus also one these men wanted rule matter how and for what end when now apuleius was tribune marius was consul for the sixth time was then that the former really began his career legislator trying win the favour the people set seditious motions his aims were quite different from those which earlier days were called seditious was striving establish tyranny design indeed which only general like sylla csar could have succeeded carrying out the legislation saturninus however has come down very obscure thus much know that most sweeping agrarian law was one its main features and that changed the giving out corn into regular distribution alms would seem the whole the lands divided his lex agraria were situated transpadane gaul for that they should have been france itself not likely said also have made lex judiciaria now flattered marius every possible way wanted found colonies and the coloni were consist romans and italians for the italian
allies the army marius had also very much distinguished themselves apuleius favoured them much the romans and this was what exasperated many the poorer roman citizens against the law marius was moreover have the power giving each these colonies the roman citizenship three italian allies thing which indeed went beyond all bounds authority yet though that time this was still something quite monstrous trenched upon some the rights the sovereign people umbrage was taken afterwards when imperator bestowed the citizenship these laws were opposed both account their author and their evident tendency all rightminded men even those who former days had with all their might withstood the oligarchy and likewise the brokendown oligarchs themselves who now wanted more than what was reasonable hence was that memmius became the object the rage the seditious though twelve years before when tribune had called upon the people quell the oligarchy had only behaved ever like honest man owing the hortensian law the new lex agraria not require the sanction the senate that that body however might not afterwards attack saturninus demanded that the senators should swear five days after its adoption the tribes and when this was debated the senate marius first declared
that ought not done that would not take the oath and that hoped that every welldisposed person would follow his example was thought that acted thus from craftiness draw his enemies particularly metellus refuse the oath likewise nor this impossible but may also have honestly meant what said though afterwards false friends began work upon him means his unhappy dread the mob cicero had the strength mind not allow himself thus overawed says speech his pro rabirio perduell nihil clamor iste commovet sed consolatur quum indicat esse quosdam cives imperitos sed non multos neither plutarch nor appian have thrown any light upon this subject the end all the laws there the following formula quid sacri sanctique est quod non jus sit rogari ejus hac lege nihil rogatur else quid jus non esset rogarier ejus lege nihilum rogatum these unlucky advisers now said that the law was not passed blood would flow but that were passed this clause would give protection against everything the body the enactment which was thus made null and void such casuistry this they got marius declare the fifth day the senate that even they took the oath they would still have this loophole left them thus
the oath was taken marius and after him all the rest except metellus numidicus who stood out against with constancy truly heroic which does him greater honour than his numidian victories and which would lead one pardon his haughtiness marius the day trial showed resolute consistency and saturninus persisting the course which had taken had him dragged out the senate his viator and outlawed him aqua igni interdicebat which went exile rhodes the year was passed horrors the stain upon marius character his weakness from henceforth always stands undecided position trimming between both factions and thus saw himself dependent upon the very storms which surrounded him good luck would have these fellows carried things far that they brought about fusion parties and marius himself not wanting have any more with them was ready declare against them the elections for the consulship were now held and antonius was unanimously chosen the following day seemed certain that memmius would elected was one the most energetic and rightminded men that age being probably the tribune jugurthas time not the same least very near kinsman his against this candidate who was all but returned glaucia and saturninus raised tumult they not however venture have

had begin making themselves popular after which they went over the opposite side thus was that domitius ahenobarbus transferred the nomination the pontificate and the other priestly offices from the colleges which used fill their own numbers the tribes and this was indeed managed that the smaller half the tribes was chosen lot the electors the earliest times the right choice undoubtedly belonged the patricians alone when however the patricians and plebeians shared these offices between them plebeians also were added the voters but afterwards when the curies were longer assembled but were become altogether changed was quite natural that the election should left the colleges themselves the clause that the lesser half the tribes was elect seems have been based old form expression the patricians when they were still existence having been called perhaps the twelve tables minor pars populi different meaning was now given this was the last trace which remained the old constitution the two questions which filled the minds every one were the courts justice and the citizenship the allies the want change the former was strongly felt the best men well the worst people like mucius scvola whose behaviour the provinces had been quite exemplaryhe

nothing had been done for them with the exception one law which the tithe from the ager publicus was abolished this however only know from appian they now urged their demands more strongly than ever and the right roman citizenship was even becoming more valuable their eyes for they were getting more and more like the romans they had learned speak the same language and yet war and peace they were subject the sway roman masters this fermentation the rulers rome were greatly terrified but whenever they came decision they only increased the irritation thus some italians had quietly taken themselves the right citizenship one them peperna had even attained the consulate and the censorship and now was found out that was not lawfully citizen the general breaking everything rome fell into confusion the calendar was the time csar owing arbitrary intercalations more than eighty days behindhand and like manner the census had been disturbed the admission allies they had assumed the character citizens and the censors had classed them the tribes now the lex mucia licinia the mad resolution was suddenly come making strict inquiries into this matter and striking off all those who were not citizens the fullest
sense the word this could not but have exasperated immense number people but the infatuation which then prevailed everywhere was inconceivable degrees however considerable party the senate became convinced that reform must take place and these were the sons the very men who had baffled the plans the gracchi they wanted make attempt remedy the evil the reform most urgently called for being change the judicial system but this was opposed all the immense influence the equites which was great make even polybius say that his times few people only had nothing with them carry this out men now thought giving the full franchise the latins and allies and this ought have been done any rate under these circumstances livius drusus the son him who during the tribuneship gracchus had gotten unhappy celebrity man uncommon talent whose hands were clean became tribune and thought upon remedies all sensible people and the chief persons the state joined with him hinder revolution means reform here again much obscure for what belongs these later ages are sometimes much more under the necessity guessing than with regard the earlier times then the form was reality being based upon numbers now had wholly lost its
meaning what most likely that statement appian after all correct according which was the chief aim drusus bring mixed system and not give back the administration justice the senators alone which would have caused revolution the lex servilia the rule had already been laid down that the judges the courts should divided between the knights and the senators but this not last long the senate consisted three hundred men and these said meant add three hundred knights from both them combined the jury was chosen lot for ever since the days gracchus there was really system like that trial jury the english antiquaries have wanted find even earlier period but they were wrong cases there were still single arbitri but for political offences and also for felony there were qustiones perpetu which were analogous the modern jury courts probable that this measure reform one half the jury must have been made senators and the other knights thus livius offered these last advantage which they might have compensation instead the exclusive exercise the judicial power this another law was tacked which qustiones were appointed inflict punishment any one who should convicted having given wrong judgment for the sake bribe from favour
what was the form these qustiones more than can tell all likelihood they were held the tribes but there were very many knights who had wish whatever the senate was much more agreeable them stand highest among those who not belong that body and instead sharing its moral responsibility always able find fault and judge seems moreover that the law drusus not enact that the three hundred each class were kept distinct for ever more likely that this filling the senate was only thought transitory measure and that eventually the judicial power was rest again with the senate the knights now said that this was neither more nor less than scheme outwit them that they would afterwards have senate six hundred into which more knights were admitted than there used but that the courts justice would taken out their hands yet the plan drusus seems after all have been the best thing that could have been done that time also meant give the citizenship the italians thus renewing the strength the higher classes bringing fresh aristocracy and enlarging the roman state into nation likewise aimed restoring the middle classes and carrying through new agrarian law favour the romans and italians

the war was not begun those who had originally planned but the peoples which lived farther off which these was the first resolve upon more than know but stated that the year during the tribuneship livius drusus there was plot kill the roman consuls philippus especially and the senate the latin feast that solemnity indeed the whole the roman magistracy consuls prtors and even tribunes the people were present that there remained behind but prfectus urbi latinarum causa who was young man rank now the latins mustered there strong numbers very probable that was they who had entertained that design especially the men tibur and prneste the same time may have happened that many italians came thither that they their part deemed the thing feasible drusus heard this atrocious project and denounced for even had not been man honour was still roman and what wanted just much for the advantage his own country from any love which bore the allies after the death drusus the italians making secret their unmitigated rage sent round ambassadors and gave each other hostages for mutual security the roman government the other hand appointed commissioners with proconsular power for picenum where the commotion was fiercest
remind the allies their duty there being what would call diet the picentines asculum the proconsul servilius cpio accompanied fonteius not exactly remember his prnomen came forward and ventured address the people induce them either exhortation threats desist from their intention but their minds were exasperated that rash word made them break out and and his companion were murdered the theatre asculum the italians now wished longer for the roman franchise but they wanted form sovereign italian people which all who got out the grasp the romans were received all the romans who were asculum were seized and most them slain the fragments diodorus among the excerpta sententiis there little story harlequin who was great favourite with the romans and who just then made his appearance the games asculum the people believing him roman were going kill him when only saved himself proving that was latin this passage instead are read the old name for pulcinella and this the first mention that mask the insurrection now broke out everywhere but the same atrocities not seem have been perpetrated among the other peoples were done the picentines asculum who were cowardly abject race the marsians and other nations were quite equal
the romans refinement the italian peoples who that time revolted are mentioned the epitome livy and orosius they are the picentines marsians marrucinians vestinians and pelignians the samnites and lucanians appian speaks also the apulians who indeed were arms but very likely that they had share the italian state those peoples fact were all them sabellians sabine colonies the others well the apulians who were oscans may have joined them merely being their dependents some the towns also round the bay naples were among those which rebelled the latin colonies venusia sided with them afterwards the umbrians likewise took arms and for short time the etruscans well but they too not belong the republic the italian peoples according appian who alone has recorded this fact had established senate five hundred persons and chosen two consuls and twelve prtors thus altogether adopting the forms the roman republic one consul was pompdius silo the soul the undertaking who was marsian and the guestfriend drusus with whom had formerly negotiated the second was papius mutilus sabine and not speak this constitution the nations were very widely distinct from each other they had been parted for centuries each standing itself that when they now
made themselves independent rome there could not but have been great temptation independent each other their principles and pursuits being different the samnites whom afterwards pontius telesinus led against rome that might said destroy the den the wolf had from old entertained implacable hatred against rome and indeed pontius telesinus himself who this war with sylla showed such undaunted resolution and whose thoughts were ever bent romes annihilation may have sprung from the gens pontia that pontius who had terribly humbled the romans caudium the marsians the other hand had never had fierce and protracted war with the romans the latter had always faithfully fulfilled their honourable conditions with them these therefore were quite heterogeneous element the league the seat the government was corfinium the country the pelignians small but valiant people and the town now assumed the name italica denarii are not unseldom found which have the inscription italia and viteliu the latter which the oscan way writing belongs the samnites the former the latin one the marsians who had language their own but latin letters from this see that those nations differed also their languages among the samnites the oscan was indeed the prevailing language the marsians and
their allies were far purer race than the sabines although wider sense the word they were all them sabines there are also coins still existing with the likeness papius mutilus the outbreak the war the allies had decidedly the advantage the only thing which saved the romans was that the latin colonies remained true them there doubt but that soon ever the struggle began the romans granted the full franchise the latins the lex julia which was called from the consul julius csar common but yet incorrect way speaking say that the italians had got the rights citizenship through the lex julia for they not get these all once one law but several distinct enactments which were successively enlarged unhappily know none their details the lex julia applied the forty fifty latin colonies and not only those italy but also narbo and aqu sexti the former mentioned later period colonia civium romanorum and without doubt tibur and prneste well besides those other old latin towns which had not received all the rights citizenship the year this last class the hernican towns especially belonged and perhaps also venafrum atina and some others which that time there was prfectura this gave great
increase the strength the romans who even the war with hannibal had thus brought into the field eighty thousand men able bear arms all whom spoke latin roman citizens likewise being mingled with them was now seen how foolish was the romans have let things far for had they turned deaf ear the latins also rome would have been lost this grant the franchise dates from the beginning the year although hiero his day had still said that the romans employed none but italian troops yet they now carried the war with soldiers raised from whatever country they could get them with gauls mauritanians numidians asiatics not place was spared the levy thus degrees the preponderance the italians was balanced the latins and outweighed last the foreigners moreover rome had immense advantage from her central position and her colonies which were scattered all over italy her position she cut off the north from the south her colonies which was everywhere necessary beset with troops the resources the allies were frittered away the history the war chiefly found diodorus and appian have been much pains about and have tried put the materials order yet have only just barely succeeded getting anything

the vestinians separated from the rest and now the romans held out allurements the nations singly granting them peace and the franchise what the conditions were know not though there must have been more than the civitas sine suffragio the romans however must have taken care not lay down distinct rule for afterwards there dispute about the meaning the grant velleius paterculus very ingenious writer who was perfectly master his subject whatever objections one may have the man himself tells that nearly three hundred thousand italians who were able bear arms perished this war and that the romans had not yielded the citizenship the italians until they had spent the last drop blood which they had shed may therefore take for granted that half the whole number men engaged both sides were killed and that therefore the struggle was carried with the greatest fury war hence appian also places his work such the second year the war still less made out than the first thus much only certain that the northern sabellian peoples also the marsians marrucinians and pelignians had now separate peace even early perhaps the end the first year these new citizens were not distributed among the old
tribes but others were formed out them this was quite keeping with the system the ancients otherwise the old citizens would have been outnumbered the assemblies the people and the elections the new ones not known for certain how many fresh tribes were created according passage velleius there were eight them another statement appian evidently written wrong there find viz from which has been gathered though perhaps would then have been better read yet from appians usual way speaking seems have been reasons for this are from feeling symmetry add have quite awkward number which had grown degrees and which one would not wish stop and therefore somewhat less than half the original number which was now necessity changed that velleius has eight account for the circumstance that the latins had eight tribes given them and afterwards the etruscans and umbrians got seven the number battles fought this war even beyond belief corfinium took again its old name and the seat government was transferred sernia the samnites now formed the real centre the war and they carried with the same perseverance they had done former times this was least the case with the three cantons the hirpinians the caudines and
the pentrians the romans marched into apulia and entirely surrounded the samnites that already the end the year the war was well nigh decided the samnites indeed still held out yet there were none arms besides them but part the apulians and lucanians these peoples went with the war from despair alone they either reckoned the movement asia caused the war mithridates they had made their minds perish this second year the war there was also rising the etruscans and the umbrians but they soon made their peace with the romans their rebellion took quite different character from that the italiansa prtor conquers the etruscans and they get the franchise once the etruscans had formerly furnished troops for the roman army yet now they were ready take arms for honour which they had not hitherto attached any value the roman rank had the marsian very dangerous rival for all the offices whereas the other hand the etruscan being foreigner quite distinct from the roman had far less chance getting these places the marsians were the romans very much like what the germans the north are those the south and therefore they readily blended with the romans whilst the etruscans were
these the french the slavonians are the germans the samnites olden times wished for the destruction rome the italian war had raised the glory sylla its highest point and now his aversion and enmity against marius showed itself conspicuously the year sylla had been elected consul the age fortynine while marius was already past seventy sylla therefore decidedly belonged later generation this utterly widened the breach which everything had existed between them sylla sulla most original character and difficult give cut and dry opinion about him was great general and also favourite fortune circumstance which himself laid great stress and which also drew the attention the crowd upon him nor delusion that some men are favoured luck either always for long run when still very young man being much under forty had distinguished himself the war jugurtha serving qustor under marius and had had the good fortune carry the negotiations with bocchus that looked upon the ending his own work had likewise won renown the cimbric and still more the italian war the which far outshone marius was the only roman who played brilliant part was the illustrious gens the cornelii and was descended the sixth generation from that cornelius
rufinus who honourably mentioned the war with pyrrhus yet the family which belonged was undistinguished the name sulla has been rightly derived gronovius from sura surula contraction sulla consequently apparent diminutive which has the same meaning the root itself sura was surname the lentuli and others was every respect the opposite marius the latter had risen from the ranks and was soldier fortune sylla the contrary was refined man the world for his chief delight was greek literature was quite master the greek language and writer elegant taste his family being poor rose from under great difficulties had been humble parentage the patrician ties were broken and the scipios and lentuli were help him marius had all the unhappy feelings old man against younger one who making his way this rising sun troubled him and made him ease and treating that extraordinary man with envy and jealousy provoked him opposition whichcertainly from marius own fault firstgave birth their mutual dislike ever since the time the war with jugurtha marius had done his best keep his rival down and sylla must also have said himself had been marius place should have done just notwithstanding his old age marius was insatiable ruling
and commanding and demanded for himself the conduct the war against mithridates which had been given sylla the consul that year the motive for this war was the very justest the side mithridates the wrong done the romans being too glaring mithridates had sprung from persian family which even early under the persian kings had its satrapy pontus the first whom know all likelihood was ariobarzanes governor those countries under ochus perhaps was one the seven noble families which alone had freedom being some sort sacrosancti and invested with the hereditary dignity governors those parts the nation consisted syrians and assyrians that say the great mass may originally have been armenian but early the times the assyrian rule over asia colony assyrians may have settled here who called themselves leucosyrians was their good fortune that alexander not devastate their country was only under his successors that they got involved the macedonian wars mithridates the son the then governor who arrogated himself the dignity tributary prince escaped the friendship demetrius poliorcetes from the jealousy antiochus the oneeyed the father demetrius these countries afterwards established their power firm footing that even the fifth century rome their governors already took the title kings
during the long wars the successors alexander particularly those the syrian kings with egypt their strength was completely consolidated but they were divided inheritance into two kingdoms cappadocia and pontus proper they were either under the same dynasty least both them subject persian families this separation still continued the beginning the seventh century about the year when mithridates ruled over pontus proper and part paphlagonia gave help the romans against aristonicus and had before that sent galleys against carthage and reward they yielded him great phrygia which until then had belonged the kingdom pergamus from fragment speech gracchus find however that had bought this grant from those who were power rome thus then his kingdom was great extent and its strength and its revenues were considerable quite different scale from that our poor europe that time lesser asia was divided into the kingdoms pontus and bithynia which the former was the largest into the roman province and into cappadocia and the southern coast where cilicia caria pamphylia and number small independent states were then chaotic confusion mithridates justly called the great had the death his fatherthe mithridates mentioned abovebeen left infant and had come the throne after hard trials though
had given provocation had very early been injured the romans who know not why took back from him that highly important possession great phrygia which his father had gained this treachery awakened him implacable feeling revenge besides his many other remarkable qualities mithridates had extraordinary talent for dissimulation and thus while seemed altogether quiet but was silently making his preparations sought widen his dominions without doing any mischief the romans conquered the cimmerian bosporus the crimea and the south the ukraine far the dnieper which gave him great accession strength soon afterwards found opportunity gaining cappadocia where there were quarrels about the succession the reigning king having been declared supposititious now placed his own son brother that throne this aroused the jealousy the romans and they set against him another pretender ever since had become age had done his utmost collect fleet and large army evidently against rome and the meanwhile reckoned the war which was raging italy nor there any doubt his being connected with the allies yet had not completed his preparations the right moment and this circumstance many other cases saved rome this time also from the impending danger had engaged this undertaking two years earlier the
beginning the social war things might indeed have taken different turn but made too sure the success the italians and believed that they would render his conquests only still more easy rome the meanwhile recovered herself from the marsian war which lingered but feebly the second year the struggle she had sent commissioners asia prescribe laws mithridates and this may have overawed him for much they had fallen off their political weight was still the same and threatened they were the greatest dangers italy they not yet lose sight asia moreover mithridates then abetted the designs brother king nicomedes bithynia whose worthless race parricide and fratricide were quite common occurrences nicomedes was expelled and mithridates became the ally the new king yet allowed himself far daunted the romans put with the restoration nicomedes bithynia and ariobarzanes cappadocia though not indeed give his plan revenge the romans however might they had wished have still kept off the war much longer and the government would perhaps have liked have done but individuals who governed the provinces and hoped gain booty would not hear peace but forced nicomedes into hostilities against mithridates that they might have opportunity coming his assistance cappadocia was not

finished slew one and the same day proof their fidelity mithridates all the romans and italians who were among them the number these said have been seventy thousand which almost beyond belief after all none but those who were well off and men business could have resided there the massacre was carried out with the greatest cruelty thus the many usurers and bloodsuckers perished who after the hard wars aristonicus had wrung the highest rates interest from the people which was need money and who backed the cohort and the protection the roman prfect had ventured upon every sort outrage and had raised the tolls and taxes most arbitrary and overbearing way mithridates met with scarcely any opposition the peninsula some maritime towns also surrendered him and thus was brought entirely the greek mannerthere are traces the magian doctrines found him except his coins which the sun and the moon are seenthe greeks looked upon him fellow countryman spite his persian descent and was received with rapture even greece itself athens unhappily allowed herself beguiled sophist the name aristion open her gates him and this fellow set himself tyrant the peloponnesus and botia went over mithridates the whole greece with

and this demanded that merula who had been chosen consul his stead should deposed this humiliation also the senate seems have yielded but octavius the other consul would not give way betook himself with small troop the janiculum having the madness think defending himself when marius and cinna entered the city which was about the end the year the bloodshed immediately began chiefly marius instigation octavius was cut down the soldiers soon they had marched and cornelius merula the flamen dialis opened his veins and died near the altar the temple jupiter marius now had himself proclaimed consul for the seventh and cinna for the second time without any election whatever had always hoped for this consulship which had been prophesied him even from child when nest with seven young eagles fell down into his lap from tree which called cicero marius oak his acquaintance also with the syrian fortune teller may have led him dwell upon the number seven which was high import among the syrians and jews was the number three with the romans the victory was followed with the fellest cruelty marius had his bodyguard freed slaves which sent out murder people all who were distinguished the

refused him valerius flaccus his colleague after the death marius had gotten the command against mithridates and had gone asia illyricum macedon and greece and himself was the eve marching into greece against sylla having formed large army near ariminum which was follow but the soldiers refused this expedition and mutiny broke out which cinna was killed after him ruled papirius carbo who not have colleague chosen was nominally consul but reality tyrant the first mithridatic war sylla returns rome his dictatorship and death the year sylla had gone achaia and thessaly that time archelaus and taxiles the generals mithridates were masters the peloponnesus and greece south thermopyl then sylla won the battle chronea from countless host asiaticsa battle which surely could not have classed among those which rested his glory for the asiatics who were hundred thousand men showed themselves cowardly ever were the troops indian princes they were indeed drawn phalanx but was true them what somebody has said with regard those ingeniously prepared dishes lent that fish even when dressed the very best cooks after all nothing but fish sylla lost but few men here and there different defence was made archelaus the pireus the walls between
the city athens and its port had been destroyed perhaps demetrius poliorcetes and early the siege antigonus gonatas the communication seems not have been free but the huge walls themistocles restored conon were still standing the pireus where there was pontic garrison archelaus gallantly held out the city the tyrant withstood the enemy with hired troops archelaus everything his power supply athens with provisions but purpose was baffled the vigilance sylla who far surpassed him talent and resources the distress the city rose such height that the inhabitants had strength left the circumference the wall amounted german mile and there were not men enough defend the town was stormed and frightful slaughter ensued the athenians had been the deadliest enemies the romans afterwards the pireus also was taken athens itself few the buildings were touched not even the walls being destroyed the pireus however the walls the noble arsenal and other buildings were completely demolished that from that time the place was like the decayed towns the north holland where the grass grows the streets pausanias found only small hamlet where had stood athens was almost depopulated and after this the saying lucan held good with regard rarus antiquis habitator
urbibus errat sylla now gained several other advantages and drove the generals the king pontus quite out europe into asia even before him valerius flaccus had come thither proconsul but had been murdered his qustor legatus flavius fimbria who took upon himself the imperium his stead mithridates thus hemmed between two armies which were hostile each other marched first against fimbria who had destroyed ilium sylla now concluded peace which almost startles ones belief mithridates abandoned all his conquests and renounced all claim paphlagonia cappadocia bithynia and phrygia thus confining himself his hereditary dominions moreover paid down two thousand talents and yielded over seventy ships war return for this sylla not insist upon his advisers being given sylla now pressed fimbria hard that took away his own life and his soldiers went over his rival who however not trust them they were contaminati cde consulis and partizans marius for most them were certainly italians enlisted against sylla the time that marius was power these soldiers still remained there under the name valeriani for many year until the days pompey and lucullus just the soldiers cann had stay long sicily after having made this peace laid fine the greeks and the

the help the governors this was the most frightful tyranny the sword itself having wasted those countries not near much usury but sylla true could not have carried his war without money sylla showed himself great indeed his house was pulled down and his property destroyed his family had been obliged fly the country his friends were either murdered driven into banishment and many these last came him entreating him return mithridates moreover would long since have concluded peace which indeed would have been less advantageous the romans but sylla wished bring the war quite end and get the most favourable terms possible first taking care the interests his country before looked his own thus now returned with victorious army which was proud him and attached him being also possession great pecuniary resources had not more than thirty thousand men whereas there were opposed him the whole the italian peninsula far gaul four hundred and fifty cohorts that say more than hundred and eighty thousand men for that time armies were counted cohorts four hundred and twenty men more rarely legions and this was party besides which had fight for its very existence containing also the samnites who could not

the beginning the seventh century terence introduced quite different manner which compared with ennius and pacuvius and plautus above all infinitely more modern already quite free from the antiquity there are good grounds for believing that his writings have never been revisedsomewhat younger was ccilius statius campanian whose comic skill and playfulness are praised cicero who however finds fault with his language his fragments especially larger one gellius give great idea him far greater poet was attius not accius nor actius either who lived great age that even cicero still knew him his was truly tragic genius and not only composed after the greek models especially after schyluswhat have left this style beautiful that may very well placed the side what the greek has writtenbut also wrote prtextat that say historical pieces the manner shakspeare which are not tied down the unities time place came much nearer the form the greek dramas than his predecessors had done least the anapsts four feet his choruses were strictly according the rules greek verse his own tragedies also the senarii and anapsts seem have been the prevailing measures and not the long verses ennius and pacuvius and though indeed the senarii are not

sertorius first roved over the sea where the romans had little power and the pirates had greatly spread then tried for some time maintain himself ivica from thence fled the lusitanians who were the sworn foes the romans and who trusted his honour and uprightness but could not stand his ground against overwhelming numbers embarked for mauritania there declared for one the two pretenders the crown and took tangier and got great deal booty was even thinking withdrawing from public life altogether and going the canary islands out the reach roman rule and live there freedom when there now came again him invitation from the lusitanians and with the hope being able achieve something the roman commanders had usual given vent their rage spain and had made the pursuit sertorius pretext for plundering sylla moreover was dead and distant province the belief that the fabric which had built would fall pieces was quite natural romans and spaniards declared for sertorius particularly the halfcitizens hybrid who being the children roman soldiers spanish women had franchise but yet considered themselves roman citizens and had roman names and also spake both roman and spanish they were the cornerstone his power the link which
connected him with the spaniards proscribed romans who had hidden themselves hitherto now came forward join him the spaniards likewise especially the celtiberians were filled with enthusiasm for him and took arms soon could look upon himself having the chief command spain proceeded according wellarranged plan change the spaniards into romans that they were take their tone from roman civilisation and roman life but not wish sacrifice any that loftiness which the spanish character had its own gathered from among the proscribed and the other romans who were scattered the provinces from among the hybrid and partly also doubt from among the noble spaniards senate three hundred members which spoken history sall fragm senatus hispanicus thus making rome out rome then established osca town the north spain the huesca the present day academy into which got together the sons the most distinguished men and had them instructed the roman language and grammar according the ancient meaning that word they were also like the young romans rank adorned with the bulla and dressed the prtexta evident that secured them the roman franchise these boys were the same time him the hostages for the fidelity the parents thing which was very necessary
